i have not see much on this before so it will be very useful to you if that be something you be interested in .
exercise selection difference exercise selection varies depend on whether you be train primarily for strength or size .
when you be train for strength you have to do specific exercise .
whether they be exercise necessary for the sport you compete in .
such as the straight bar back squat , flat barbell bench press and conventional / sumo deadlift in powerlifting .
or just lift that be a good benchmark of general strength capability even if they be not part of a sport you compete in .
these may include weighted pull ups , weight dip and front squat .
they may easily irritate connective tissue and not stimulate the muscle well for the amount of fatigue they cause .
because these lift be use as benchmark , to get the most out of them you will have to train them .
this allow you to get the skill of the lift down to see where your actual strength lie .
you may have to incorporate certain lift that be not an efficient use of your time / recovery resource .
for hypertrophy there be no mandatory lift .
there be at least several different exercise variation and often many movement pattern that can be use to stimulate every part of each muscle .
you can select exercise that seem to give you the most stimulus for the least fatigue so you can stimulate as much as possible while limit fatigue build up .
hypertrophy focus program will usually include more machine base and isolation single joint lift that use less muscle group .
more of a focus in hypertrophy training than in strength training .
strength focus program will usually include more free weight / bodyweight exercise and multi joint compound movement that allow for more free movement , unlike machine .
hybrid strength and hypertrophy program will be somewhere in between depend on which you be prioritize .
rpe difference as you get more advanced set need to be take to a relatively high rpe to be effective for muscle growth .
set below rpe 6/6.5 or so be not very effective for stimulate hypertrophy .
not that they be ineffective .
they be just not a very efficient .
your time and energy would be good spent at a slightly high rpe if your goal be just hypertrophy .
there be a minimum intensity ( percent 1rm ) to stimulate noticeable strength gain but it be not that high .
75 percent be usually consider the low bound , 80 percent be definitely heavy enough to stimulate strength well .
you could do several single at 80 percent , get a good strength stimulus and still have the hard single still be far below rpe 6. this would be a good way to stimulate strength without stimulate much hypertrophy .
however it be very rare for someone to want to maximize strength while seek absolutely 0 hypertrophy .
this rarely occur unless someone competes in a strength sport and have maxed out their weight class .
most people want a combination of strength and muscle mass .
include some low rpe strength work ( to maximize technical proficiency under heavy load and train the nervous system ) and also some high rpe hypertrophy work be a good way to accomplish both .
the ratio of which can be determine by how important each aspect be to you .
training frequency difference there be 2 different type of training frequency to consider , frequency of train each muscle group and how many day you train per week .
hypertrophy training be more suited to a high number of training day per week .
it be not uncommon for bodybuilder to train 6 day a week .
sometimes this include 2 session per day .
it be very rare for powerlifters to train 6 day per week , 5 be usually the high you will see .
strength training be a lot more neurologically tax due to the heavy load lift .
even when the volume use be not very high it be not possible for most people to get amped up to lift very heavy more than 5 day a week .
i highly doubt he train hard 6 day a week your joint and connective tissue integrity be another variable that have to be consider .
maximal strength training require you to practice specific lift , this practice also need to be heavy .
this mean you need to repeat the same movement pattern relatively frequently with heavy load .
this make it pretty easy to irritate connective tissue if you be not careful with the rest of your programming .
bodybuilding training can use a wider variety of exercise at light load which be more joint friendly .
training frequency per muscle group be quite variable for both .
especially if we consider technically focused session , these be often include in strength program to improve technical efficiency .
when discuss overload session for both you can train more frequently for hypertrophy than for strength .
this be because for hypertrophy train the muscle just need to be at least close to fully recover to overload again .
for strength all of the muscle , connective tissue and nervous system need to be close to fully recover .
the muscular system recover the fast out of these .
overload strength session ca not take place as frequently as overload hypertrophy session .
you have to maximize proficiency with a single lift when it come to strength , this be not true to the same extent for hypertrophy .
this mean you can utilize a large degree of exercise variation for hypertrophy which also allow you to train more frequently .
a good way to combine both each week be to have a strength session for each lift and 1 or more hypertrophy focus session .
these should be spread out so that you be as close to fully recover as possible for the strength session .
you can be slightly fatigue go into the hypertrophy session and still get a good hypertrophy stimulus .
progression difference progression for strength and for hypertrophy be similar but not exactly the same .
you will want to increase performance over time for both ( progressive overload ) but this will manifest in slightly different way for each .
for strength increase load be good than increase reps. it be definitely good than increase set ( volume ) which might actually be counterproductive .
for hypertrophy increase load and rep be both viable tool as long as the rep do not drop too low ( below 5 ) .
increase set ( volume ) throughout a mesocycle be debatable .
i find a good compromise to be keep set for main compound static and increase myo rep cluster on isolation lift .
this allow slight increase in volume without add noticeable fatigue from week to week which would impair strength .
the best way to combine both be to have a strength base day and hypertrophy base day for each movement pattern in each training week ( microcycle ) .
on the strength base day we prioritize load increase as long as rep do not drop too low .
on the hypertrophy base day we can try to increase load ( as long as rep do not drop too low ) .
we can also try to increase rep with the same load .
myo rep cluster on isolation movement can be slightly increase every week as long as the strength base day be not affect .
if not they can remain constant , or just be increase in place where there be enough recovery time after to not affect the strength work .
loading and rep range difference hypertrophy be pretty similar when take to failure in all rep range across the 5 - 30 rep range .
this do not mean that set under 5 rep do not stimulate hypertrophy , they absolutely do .
just that as the rep get low below 5 the set become less stimulative on a per set basis .
squat single be not the best for hypertrophy try to get compound exercise volume from purely set of 5 and below would be great for strength but poor for hypertrophy .
on a pure set for set basis they would be less stimulative .
you would also be able to do less set as you ca not handle as much heavy volume as moderate volume .
when lift very heavy there be also the risk of alter your technique slightly to be able to move more load .
the target muscle would be stimulate even less .
strength be not technically tie to a rep range .
it be purely base on how heavy you be lift relative to your one rep max ( 1rm ) .
however this be manifest in the rep range that you use .
the low the rep the heavy you can lift .
your strength base will be build most effectively with set of around 6 rep and below , however set of 7 - 10 be still effective for strength .
we can combine both of these by have both a strength and hypertrophy session for each muscle group / movement pattern throughout the week .
the strength session can be in the 4 - 7 rep range ( mainly the low end ) , which be very good for strength and be decent enough for hypertrophy .
the hypertrophy session can be in the 7 - 10 rep range which all very good for hypertrophy and decent enough for strength .
volume difference from the research available it be generally agree upon that we want to train with as much volume as we can recover from to maximize hypertrophy .
this do not necessarily mean we need to increase volume throughout a mesocycle .
high volume train contributes massively to fatigue level .
so we ca not have the volume too high otherwise our top end strength will be limit by fatigue level .
we will not effectively be able to train for strength .
this seem like a conundrum , how do we reconcile these two seemingly contradictory condition ?
diminish return , which we discuss at the start .
if the maximal amount of hypertrophy occurs at 100 percent volume , you may get 85 percent hypertrophy at 65 percent volume .
this 65 percent volume will lead to noticeably less fatigue .
if it be distribute intelligently over the week this will allow you to get a significant majority of the hypertrophy available .
it will also minimally impact your top end strength work .
this still allow you to drive your low rep range strength up due to lower fatigue level .
design hybrid strength and hypertrophy mesocycles i recently publish an article on the negative of train with high volume .
at the end of that article i briefly give some main consideration that you should abide by when create hybrid strength and hypertrophy mesocycles .
i will break it down in more detail here so you know how to structure your own hybrid strength and hypertrophy training .
consideration these be the consideration i post in my other article link above .
volume should be moderate .
the week will be asymmetrical in term of stress .
the heavy strength day should be at the very start of the week .
the middle / early end of the week should be more volume focus .
the end of the week should be easy to recover from so you be pretty fresh for the heavy day ( whether this be from easy workout or more rest day ) .
the volume ( set count ) in each week should be relatively constant .
the exception be the end of the final week of the block .
you can increase volume here since there be a deload come up .
volume volume ca not be too high or too low .
volume that be too high come with significant amount of fatigue that will affect your top end strength .
heavy strength base volume ( 80 - 85 percent ) also tend to be more difficult to recover from than moderate volume due to the sheer load be use .
if the volume be too low you simply will not have enough volume to stimulate hypertrophy at a reasonable rate if you be fairly advanced .
recently there be be a lot of debate on whether increase volume throughout a training mesocycle be optimal for hypertrophy .
i have try both keep volume ( in term of hard set ) constant and increase them slowly throughout a mesocycle .
it be hard to say if increasing volume through a mesocycle be well for hypertrophy .
i have find success increase it very slowly .
it be easy to increase too fast and run yourself into the ground .
i do not think your body adapts to a give volume level quickly enough to justify quicker increase in volume .
an increase from say 10 set of chest to 16 throughout a training block be probably overkill and can even hold back your long term progress .
rapid volume progression definitely be not the way to go with hybrid training .
the fatigue from rapid set increase will absolutely hinder how much you can lift on your strength base day .
i find increase myo rep cluster throughout a mesocycle for small easy to recover isolation movement to be the best way to increase volume over a mesocycle .
the fatigue increase from this be minimal .
it may take you from 10 set to 11/12 throughout a mesocycle use only movement that be easy to recover from .
this can also be do on hybrid program as the fatigue be minimal .
the cluster could even be increase at an even slow rate such as every other week .
in the final week of the mesocycle , even on main compound volume can be increase slightly in the second half of the week .
this be because the strength base work have already be complete , and there be a deload come up to drop any extra fatigue generate .
asymmetrical stress you need to be relatively fresh with minimal fatigue on your strength base day .
we need a certain amount of volume to drive hypertrophy , but it need to be place in a way that it do not disrupt your heavy day too much .
the goal should be increase performance on all day from week to week .
at the very least it should be increase on your strength base day if it be hold constant ( in the short term ) on your more volume focus day .
let take an example of an upper / lower split to make thing simple .
this could be accomplish by train heavy upper and low on day 1 and 2 respectively .
moderate upper low on day 4 and 5 respectively .
have day 3,6 and 7 as rest day .
keep volume ( in term of hard set ) the same on both day would give you an extra rest day for each muscle group before the strength day .
this be fine .
you can still get enough volume and intensity on the moderate day to stimulate hypertrophy .
with high frequency this can still be do , you just have to think a bit more .
for example if you be train a muscle 3x a week .
such as train the pressing muscle on day 1,3 and 5 , you may divide the set roughly equally but bias day 1 and 5 a bit .
7 set on day 1 and 5 , 6 set on day 3. day 1 would be the strength base day , day 3 and 5 would be more volume focus .
day 3 would include movement that favor short muscle length , so that there be minimal / no soreness / muscle damage for day 5. day 5 may have movement that stress long muscle length which lead to a bit more stimulation and soreness .
due to the 50 percent extra recovery time you can still recover in time for next week be day 1. this can be do with even high frequency , you just need to keep the general principle here in mind .
mesocycle design i be go to use the example above of a 4x a week upper low split and show how i would design the upper body day throughout a mesocycle .
i do not want to make this article obscenely long so i will just show the upper body progression .
you can 100 percent get the concept from what i be go to show you without the low body aspect .
do not get too attach to the specific exercise variation , set and weight use .
this be a super generic training block .
the idea be to just show how thing progress throughout the course of a mesocycle .
the main point to take away be that : the weight and rpe ( proximity to failure ) increase slightly every week .
volume ( hard set ) stay constant for the main compound ( no set change from week to week bar deload ) .
volume increase very slowly for less fatiguing isolation in the form of myo rep cluster .
this be not mandatory , they can be keep constant as well .
there be slight undulation throughout the week in term of load use .
there be enough variation in load to gain the benefit of daily undulating periodisation ( dup ) .
average rep range for compound be around 7 rep per set , and be high for isolation in the form of myo reps. on the heavy day bar the deload , most of the load use in the compound will be in the 77.5 - 87.5 percent range .
this be great for strength .
the rep be also high enough to be effective per set for hypertrophy ( there be not many set below 5 rep ) .
the isolation in the form of myo rep be light enough to ensure you be still target the correct muscle ( would be hard to do lateral raise and target the side delts with set of 6 ) .
on the strength base day the myos be just heavy enough to get a small strength stimulus ( think that be not the main purpose of isolation lift ) .
they be still in an appropriate rep range for hypertrophy .
on the strength day when do multiple set not every set have to be in the rpe range .
early set can be slightly below the target rpe to accumulate less fatigue .
the final set should always be in the range to ensure you be not too far from failure .
conclusion as long as you take into consideration the information in this article you can program for strength and hypertrophy at the same time .
you will not 100 percent optimise either but will get the best of both world , which i believe be what plenty of lifter actually want .
i find it to be a more enjoyable way to train as well .
< END > < START > conventional wisdom suggest that your pathway to success in the gym be narrow and linear .
if you want to get strong , you have to train for strength .
want to build muscle ?
hypertrophy have to be your only priority .
while this may be more true than false , especially the high you climb on your fitness journey , the reality be not as black - and - white .
powerlifters could learn a thing or two from their pose - trunk - clad colleague , and bodybuilder should not shy away from strength .
man perform standard back squat in gym if you want to enjoy the best of both world , you will need a handy guide to light your way .
here be how to mix powerlifting with bodybuilding and actually pull it off .
combine powerlifting and bodybuilding like most type of program design , there be more than one way to skin the cat .
if you want to mold your powerlifting workout to accommodate some pump work , or want to bodybuild while also get strong , your best bet be to develop an understanding of the principle at play .
do : decide your priority combine the two sport do not necessarily mean double your workload or perform both in equal measure .
instead , you should clearly define which of the two will be your “ primary ” focus .
decide whether you want to supplement your powerlifting training with bodybuilding , or vice versa , and proceed accordingly .
do not : stretch yourself thin once you have figure out which of the two will be your main focus , remember to program accordingly .
if you attempt to cover all the base in either sport or run two full routine in tandem , you might stretch or overwork yourself .
mix two style of training be all about manage your volume , effort , and expectation equally .
do : utilize different equipment mix up your training be the perfect time to dabble in different equipment .
if you be primarily a powerlifter who want to add some physique work to your training , you have a prime opportunity to utilize dumbbell , kettlebells , or cable during your accessory exercise .
conversely , if you bodybuild , train like a powerlifter will help acclimate you to the rigor of heavy barbell training in a way you may not already be familiar with .
do not : stray too far from the barbell no matter how you be go to organize your combined training , remember to include the barbell in at least some portion of your weekly regime .
barbell work can serve as the bridge between powerlifting and bodybuilding .
for powerlifters , it be a necessary facet of the sport .
for bodybuilder , barbell training be often the bedrock of both classic and modern muscle - building routine .
do : continue to compete you should continue to compete in powerlifting even if you be mix in some bodybuilding work .
regular competition , even if you “ train through ” them ( as in , not specifically peak for a performance on the day ) , keep you in tune with the atmosphere of a powerlifting meet .
on the other hand , a bodybuilder may not be able to properly prep for a show while train like a powerlifter , especially if they be not diet down .

do not : have unrealistic expectation whether you choose to compete while mix modality , you should keep your expectation in check .
most athlete , whether they train for strength or size , will perform at their best if they focus squarely on one or two specific goal .
as such , you should not necessarily expect to hit a lifetime personal record in the squat if a third of your training involve isolated hypertrophy work .
do : focus on nutrition diversify your training be no excuse to let yourself be lazy about nutrition .
powerlifters need to stay on top of their intake if they want to make a specific weight class .
bodybuilder must track their nutrition to cut down for a show or bulk up in the off - season .
therefore , it be just as important to be mindful of your eat habit even if you be not specifically work towards a weight or body composition - related goal .
do not : aim for perfection it be essential that you not get in your own way when you combine powerlifting and bodybuilding .
while you may be able to make significant gain after you acclimate to your new program , thing will likely feel a bit rocky in the beginning .
as long as you be enjoy your workout , the gain will follow .
do : periodize your training although powerlifters and bodybuilder have different approach to structure their training , both rely on some form of periodization .
if you decide to add one to the other , you should still periodize your workout to ensure that your training be structure and productive .
competitive powerlifter prepares to unrack squat attempt haphazardly throw bodybuilding work into your routine be a good way to run into a plateau or induce unwanted level of fatigue .
do not : try to peak it may seem obvious , but you should not try to peak if you be mix bodybuilding into your powerlifting training or vice - versa .
a powerlifter who be go heavy on accessory work may have too much fatigue accumulate from bodybuilding work to properly peak for heavy single - rep set .
similarly , too much heavy barbell work could make you too tire to effectively focus on your subsequent bodybuilding movement .
sample workout for combine powerlifting and bodybuilding the hard part of combine two different modality be ensure that the two style of train work synergistically .
you do not want your powerlifting work to negatively impact your bodybuilding exercise , or vice - versa .
fortunately , the best way to mix the two discipline be more straightforward than you might think .
here be a general overview : powerlifting focus add hypertrophy work to your powerlifting routine be easy .
all you will need to do be dial back a little bit on your sport - specific training while still put it first chronologically and philosophically .
for example , a “ low body ” strength train workout with some leg hypertrophy build in might look something like this : back squat : 5 x 3 deficit speed pull : 6 x 2 hip thrust : 3 x 8 walk lunge : 2 x 10 step per leg leg extension machine : 2 x 15 this kind of workout put the most important and technical exercise at the front , ensure that you get high - quality practice in .
afterward , you can expand your horizon with different equipment and auxiliary movement that be well suit for grow your wheel .
note : if you follow a template program for powerlifting , you should be able to transplant the set - rep progression for your competition movement into a “ hybrid ” routine .
pay attention to how it affect your overall training quality and fatigue level .
bodybuilding focus get strong while build your body be all about balance your fatigue .
your training will generally look similar to that of a powerlifter who add bodybuilding work , but your specific workout should have a tight focus than , say , “ pull ” or “ low body .
” for example : rack or block pull : 8 x 3 kroc row : 3 x 6 wide - grip lat pulldown : 3 x 8 , 12 , 15 dumbbell pullover : 3 x 12 - 15 face pull : 2 x 15 - 20 this back workout will torch your lat , trap , and erectors , but it also help you develop your deadlift lockout and general pull power .
more importantly , your bodybuilding workout should be just that — center around build your body .
the bench press , squat , and deadlift ( or their many variation ) should accompany the same body part you be hit on that day .
you might find it difficult to properly train your chest for mass if you start your workout with heavy back squat .
method you can look beyond individual workout and toward your overall training week if you want to combine powerlifting with bodybuilding as well .
one alternative method of combination program design involve dedicate one day solely to powerlifting or strength - specific work , and then perform a physique - focus workout on a separate day .
for example , this two - day leg train scheme put that idea into practice : day one ( strength focus ) back squat : 5 x 5 deadlift : 3 x 3 good morning : 2 x 10 weighted plank : 2 x 30 second day two ( hypertrophy focus ) front squat : 6 x 3 romanian deadlift : 3 x 6 , 8 , 12 bulgarian split squat : 3 x 8 - 10 leg extension : 2 x 15 leg curl : 2 x 15 calf raise : 3 x 15 you be still train legs twice per week .
in fact , you be also squat twice to ensure high - quality skill development .
the key difference be that both workout have a distinct and clear focus , and should also “ feel ” quite different from each other .
the first session be par - for - the - course powerlifting , while the subsequent workout train a variation of the competitive back squat and then hammer your leg with all manner of accessory work .
benefit of combine powerlifting and bodybuilding you might not get as strong as a career powerlifter who only care about their total .
in the same vein , full - time physique development be probably the best way to bulk up .
however , there be some unique benefit to mix your method and dabble in both powerlifting and bodybuilding simultaneously .
big muscle be strong muscle there be a synergistic relationship between muscular cross - sectional area ( which be to say , how jacked you be ) and strength potential .
if you remove other factor like technical efficiency , train experience , or fatigue , a big muscle will be strong than a small one .
( 1 ) ( 2 ) muscle reduces injury risk there be no foolproof way of 100 percent eliminate the risk of injury in the gym .
luckily , strength training be not particularly injurious , especially when compare to ballistic exercise or contact sport .
( 3 ) however , add muscle to your frame may help reduce the risk of injury or sport - related accident in the gym , at least partially .
( 4 ) strength help you grow powerlifting be all about teach you to push your limit .
after all , you ca not casually set a new 1 - rep max .
as such , the sport - specific demand of powerlifting might also help you be a good bodybuilder .
there be a dose and , particularly , effort - response relationship between resistance training and hypertrophy .
put simply , the long you have be in the gym , the harder you will need to work to grow .
( 5 ) high - intensity strength training will teach you to apply effort across the board , instead of sandbag your “ small ” isolation exercise .
more novelty to your workout dedicate and focus programming be a fantastic way to hit a specific goal .
on the other hand , strict periodization — whether you be try to add pound to your bar or inch to your arm — be monotonous by nature .
if repetitive workout tend to make you feel bore or burn out , mix up your method can remedy the issue and keep you move forward at the same time .
there be no harm in enjoy variety in the gym .
your takeaway to succeed at the absolute high level of any athletic discipline , you will probably have to specialize .
bar that , it be both possible ( and potentially beneficial ) to combine powerlifting and bodybuilding into one comprehensive training plan .
understand that you will not be able to perform both as well as if you would focus solely on either .
keep the barbell in the limelight , but do not be afraid to experiment with non - sport - specific exercise while you can .
if you be a strength or physique athlete , it might be wise to compete casually during period of combination training .
put your strength work first during your workout , or dedicate an entire day to it exclusively .
the physiological effect of combination training can benefit you whether you prefer powerlifting or bodybuilding .
big muscle be strong muscle , and the musculoskeletal stimulation of bodybuilding can make you a more robust and resilient strength specialist .
strength , size , and a whole lot more if you follow bodybuilding , you might notice a recent trend — a lot of the top athlete be not afraid to lift heavy in the gym .
many , in fact , credit max - effort training as a boon to their physique development .
conversely , the modern powerlifter be not afraid to look the part .
many of the strong athlete in the world be jack out of their mind , and rightly so .

not necessarily .

absolutely not .

long distance run so , if you enjoy run and want to make this part of your exercise routine , be long - distance run or sprint best ?
long - distance run vs sprinting : what be the difference ?
first , figure out the difference between long - distance running and sprint before go far .
what be long - distance run ?
many people think of long - distance run as marathon and cross - country race , which certainly count as long - distance running , but it do not have to be long .
anything that involve run for two mile or more can be consider long - distance .
it require stamina , aerobic endurance , and mental toughness .
it be the chosen run for those with more time on their hand and who enjoy take time out to reset their body and mind .
what be sprint ?
sprinting be run flat over a short distance so that you be anaerobic and finish the exercise out of breath .
it be an all - out effort design to test your lung to their maximum capacity .
the benefit of sprint include improvement in speed , blood pressure , and cardiovascular health .
this should be an exercise you can complete in under 30 second .
the idea be that you will recover afterward and repeat several time .
the recovery time between group will depend on how fit you be , but ideally , it should give you enough time to get your breathe back to relative normality , between 1.5 and 2 minute be ideal .
long - distance run vs sprinting : which help you lose more weight ?
there be an argument for both discipline , for sure .
both long - distance and sprint be exercise that will get you move , and your body will know it be be in a workout at the end , so there be plenty to suggest that both will burn enough calorie to make a marked improvement in body composition .
be long - distance run good for weight loss ?
when you think about lose weight , long - distance running be probably one of the first place your mind go .
after all , you do not see many overweight long - distance runner – so it must work .
however , it be not always the most effective way to burn calorie , especially consider the time it take .
as a general rule , an average - sized runner will burn about 100 calorie per mile .
so , if you want to burn 500 calorie , you need to run around 5 mile .
at an average pace , five mile would take around 50 minute to run , although realistically , it would take you long if you be new to run .
so , theoretically , you could burn load of calorie and be in a calorie deficit , but only if you have lot of time to run .
long - distance running be a great way to get your muscle move at a speed that suit you , get your heart rate up and build strength and endurance .
if you be new to exercise , your body increase its sensitivity to insulin , which mean you can use carbohydrate more efficiently and burn fat .
this mean that , to begin with , long - distance running could be an effective way to lose weight .
however , your body be just too damn clever ; over time , it adapt to whatever new stress be throw at it and the stimulus become more effortless .
this mean that eventually you will burn few calorie over the same distance , and hard it will be to lose weight .
plus , long - distance run can leave you feel starve afterward .
the temptation to eat more sugary or high - cal food as a treat need to be avoid .
otherwise , you be cancel out the workout .
when be long - distance run good for weight loss ?
if you be new to exercise or live a sedentary lifestyle , jog or long - distance running be an effective way to lose weight .
however , this will taper off once your body adapts , and fat and weight loss will plateau .
be sprint good for weight loss short burst of sprint be over so quickly that you might not realize just how great they can be for burn calorie and fat .
a 2019 study conclude that high - intensity sprint interval training result in a 28.5 percent high fat reduction .
you can burn up to 500 calorie by run 10 x 100 - meter sprint , and the entire session will take around twenty minute , which be perfect to incorporate into a busy schedule .
however , warm up be still essential .
go from zero to full speed from a cold start will put immense pressure on your joint , muscle , and heart .
it be vital to take up your heart rate progressively .
start with some stretch and star jump .
make sure you be work your hamstring and quad ( gently , of course- do not put massive pressure on them during the warm - up ) .
when be sprint good for weight loss ?
sprinting be excellent for weight loss and be most likely one of the most effective exercise you can do .
however , it be high - intensity and put great stress on your body – so it be not something beginner will likely be able to do immediately .

whether you intend to concentrate on high or low - intensity workout , you need to get your body use to what you will be ask it to do .

long - distance run vs sprint : at the end of each session , try eight to ten stride .

if you be new to sprinting , try eight to ten sprint per session , and increase gradually as you get strong .
the key to burn calorie be not the number of set ; it be the intensity of the sprint , so that should be your primary focus .
as the week and month progress , you can increase the intensity by reduce the recovery time between rep and add gradient , so you run slightly uphill .

should you run long - distance or sprint ?

< END > < START > once a workout be over and you be back in your daily routine , your body be metabolism can continue to burn more calorie then when at complete rest .
this physiological effect be call excess post - exercise oxygen consumption also know as oxygen debt , epoc be the amount of oxygen require to restore your body to its normal , rest level of metabolic function ( call homeostasis ) .
it also explain how your body can continue to burn calorie long after you have finish your workout .
your metabolism be how your body convert the nutrient you consume in your diet to adenosine triphosphate ( atp ) , the fuel your body use for muscular activity .
atp be produce either with oxygen use the aerobic pathway or without oxygen rely on the anaerobic pathway .
when you first start to exercise , your body use the anaerobic energy pathway and store atp to fuel that activity .
a proper warm - up be important because it can take about five to eight minute to be able to efficiently use aerobic metabolism to produce the atp necessary to sustain physical activity .
once a steady - state of oxygen consumption be achieve , the aerobic energy pathway be able to provide most of the atp need for the workout .
exercise that place a great demand on the anaerobic energy pathway during the workout can increase the need for oxygen after the workout , thereby enhance the epoc effect .
here be seven thing you should know about epoc and how it can help you achieve optimal level of calorie burn from your workout .
To note , hiit be High intensity interval training , ATP be Adenosine Triphosphate , epoc be Excess Post-Exercise Oxygen Consumption , VO2 be Volume Oxygen Consumption .
: 1. during the immediate post - exercise recovery period , oxygen be use for the following function : production of atp to replace the atp use during the workout re - synthesis of muscle glycogen from lactate restore oxygen level in venous blood , skeletal muscle blood and myoglobin work with protein for the repair of muscle tissue damage during the workout restore body temperature to resting level 2. exercise that consume more oxygen burn more calorie the body expend approximately 5 calorie of energy ( a calorie be the amount of energy require to heat 1 liter of water 1 degree centigrade ) to consume 1 liter of oxygen .
therefore , increase the amount of oxygen consume both during and after a workout can increase the number of net calorie burn .
3. circuit training and heavy resistance training with short rest interval require atp from the anaerobic pathway , lead to a significant epoc effect strength training with compound , multi - joint weightlifting exercise or do a weightlift circuit that alternate between upper- and low - body movement place a great demand on the involved muscle for atp from the anaerobic pathway .
increase need for anaerobic atp also create a great demand on the aerobic system to replenish that atp during the rest interval and the post - exercise recovery process .
heavy training load or short recovery interval increase the demand on the anaerobic energy pathway during exercise , which yield a great epoc effect during the post - exercise recovery period .
4. high - intensity interval training ( hiit ) be the most effective way to stimulate the epoc effect the body be most efficient at produce atp through aerobic metabolism ; however , at high intensity when energy be need immediately , the anaerobic pathway can provide the necessary atp much more quickly .
this be why we can only sustain high - intensity activity for a brief period of time — we simply run out of energy .
hiit work because atp be produce by the anaerobic pathway during high - intensity exercise ; once that atp be exhaust , it be necessary to allow atp to be replenish .
the rest interval or active - recovery period during an anaerobic workout allow aerobic metabolism to produce and replace atp in the involved muscle .
the oxygen deficit be the difference between the volume of oxygen consume during exercise and the amount that would be consume if energy demand be meet through only the aerobic energy pathway .
5. epoc be influence by the intensity , not the duration of exercise high intensity require atp from anaerobic pathway .
if the atp require to exercise at a particular intensity be not obtain aerobically , it must com3e from the anaerobic pathway .
during epoc , the body use oxygen to restore muscle glycogen and rebuild muscle protein damage during exercise .
even after a hiit workout be over , the body will continue to use the aerobic energy pathway to replace the atp consume during the workout , thus enhance the epoc effect .
6. research have show that resistance training can provide a great epoc effect than run at a steady speed in an extensive review of the research literature on epoc , study conclude that “ study in which similar estimate energy cost or similar exercise vo2 have be use to equate continuous aerobic exercise and intermittent resistance exercise , have indicate that resistance exercise produce a great epoc response .
” for example , one study find that when aerobic cycling ( 40 minute at 80 percent max hr ) , circuit weight training ( 4 sets/8 exercises/15 rep at 50 percent 1 - rm ) and heavy resistance exercise ( 3 sets/8 exercise at 80 - 90 percent 1 - rm to exhaustion ) be compare , heavy resistance exercise produce the big epoc .
7. the epoc effect from a hiit or high - intensity strength - training workout can add 6 to 15 percent of the total energy cost of the exercise session high - intensity workouts require more energy from the anaerobic pathway and can generate a great epoc effect , lead to extend post - exercise energy expenditure .
heavy weight training and hiit workout appear to be superior to steady - state running or low - intensity circuit training in create epoc ( , withers and , 2006 ) .
admittedly there be some debate about the significance of the epoc effect for the average exercise participant because the high - intensity exercise require for epoc can be extremely challenging .
however , if you want result and be up for the challenge , increase the intensity of your workout by use heavy weight , short rest interval or high - intensity cardio interval may be worth the effort .
while hiit or heavy resistance training be effective and beneficial , remember to allow at least 48 hour of recovery time between high - intensity exercise session and try to limit yourself to no more than three strenuous workout per week .
if you do start increase the intensity of your workout to boost epoc , consider add these recovery strategy .

that mean begin the session with sprint work before get into any strength work for the day .
a third place to add a short sprint session to a training plan be during what be know as a quota day .
a quota day be typically a shorter , easy run at the end of a week that an athlete us to fulfill weekly mileage quota .
these typically fall the day after a long run , and two day before a quality interval session .
the timing suggestion for add these sprint session be to ensure a full day of recovery from any other hard session prior to and directly follow the workout .
this ensure full recovery before a workout that induce heavy tissue damage .
again , follow the sequencing as if you be add these to base building run where the sprint session be include at the beginning of a run .
it be all about priority and make sure you do not come into a sprint session with per - fatigue muscle and risk injury .
speed training option there be two different sprint skill that require training , and they have different session characteristic .
those skill be acceleration , or the ability to gain speed in a short amount of time , and maximal velocity , or the high possible sprint speed you can achieve .
to train for acceleration , you can use a variety of method that include short distance sprint acceleration , resist run , or hill sprint .
the goal should be to keep each repetition at or under 30 m and to allow for around 1 minute of rest for each 10 m of sprint or 1:20 to 1:40 work to rest ratio .
total volume for a session should not exceed 300 m and take into consideration athlete experience level , total training volume , and time constraint .
acceleration workout session : perform the following set and rep at a max effort level , and use a two point start position .
a two point start position be start with both foot on the ground in a stance similar to a football wide receiver prior to the snap .
for athlete with injury history or return from injury , use a “ drop - in ” to start ( a skip into the sprint start ) to reduce the force of start from stand .
5 time at 10 m w/ 1 minute rest 2 minute rest then into 4 time at 20 m w/ 2 minute rest 4 time at 30 m w/ 2 minute rest to train for maximal velocity , you can use method that include assisted sprint , fly start , and sprint - float - sprint .
the goal should be to keep each repetition at or under 60 m and to allow for between 2 to 4 minute of rest between rep or 1:20 to 1:40 work to rest ratio .
total volume for a session should not exceed 300 m. maximal velocity workout session : 6 time at 15 m fly sprint with 30 m run - in w/ 2 minute rest sprint training can seem like an incredibly daunt world to venture into for endurance athlete , but it do not have to be complex to be effective .
as study have prove , this can be one of the most beneficial training session for endurance athlete at all level .
it require very little time and even less equipment .
just start small and build these session into your training plan as the body adapts .
most importantly , have fun with it .
run really fast on a field or a track will make you feel like a pro athlete , and it beat run that same neighborhood loop for the billionth time .
more importantly , it will make you a fast runner and run fast be essentially the goal whether that be over a distance of 100 meter or 100 mile .
so , get out there and channel your inner usain bolt .
who know , maybe you be a sprinter all along .
< END > < START > a runner be typical week of training involve workout at a variety of pace , range from slow , easy run for recovery and basic aerobic endurance to threshold effort and race - pace interval to build fitness for a specific race distance .
but perhaps the least - used pace in the average runner be train be the fast one — sprint training .
while some runner include a couple of stride once a week to keep in touch with their speed , do true sprint workout on a regular basis be not very popular .
while this might make sense , as only the last hundred meter or so of a distance race involve actually sprint , the usefulness of train all - out speed nevertheless merit some scientific investigation .
can sprint train substitute hard work ?
sprint train get something of a bad rap as a shortcut for quick result .
this be somewhat deserved , give the amount of people tout it as a total replacement for old - fashion hard work .
give what we already know from the collective wisdom of thousand of runner put in traditional training over many year , sprint training will never be a true replacement for easy running , aerobic workout , and race - specific work , but could prove to be a useful addition to our train regimen , depend on what the science say .
while there have be plenty of study on the use of sprint training ( narrowly define here as short , high - intensity interval at speed well over that of your usual race distance ) in untrained people , which usually show that these “ high - intensity interval training ” or hiit session be quite effective at get short - term result , we be only interested in the effect of sprint training in well - trained runner or endurance athlete .
instead of focus on whether sprint training be superior to any other kind , we should instead take note of what effect it have on fitness so we can predict when and how to integrate it into training .
sprint training and fitness their study investigate the muscular adaptation that occur in response to six session of sprint training ( 4 - 7 x 30 second all - out with four minute recovery ) spread out over two week .
use eight reasonably fit cyclist , they measure a variety of muscular parameter before and after the six interval training session , compare them to change in a control group which do not do any sprint training .
after the two - week training intervention , the cyclist show a significant increase in muscular marker for store and process fuel during exercise .
however , they have no change in their vo2 max , the amount of oxygen they use during exercise .
the performance of the cyclist in a ride - to - exhaustion improve dramatically as well , move from 26 minute until exhaustion to 51 minute .
the lack of improvement in vo2 max implies that most or all of the improvement in the rider fitness come from improvement in muscular efficiency and energy production , instead of the cardiovascular improvement observe when an athlete do traditional endurance training .
sprint training and performance the specific of how sprint training elicits improvement in the muscle be examine in more detail .
before and after seven train runner undergo a six - week train program of workout with 5 - 15 second sprint , they measure the level of biological marker of fast , anaerobic athletic performance in the athlete muscle .
like with study , the athlete show a significant improvement in time and distance cover over a run to exhaustion .
they link these improvement to increased level of a specific type of protein in the muscle call the monocarboxylate transporter 1 , or mct1 .
this protein function as a “ shuttle ” to move lactate in and out of your muscle during exercise , transport it from your leg to less - stress area where it can be reuse as fuel .
this could explain why short program of sprint training appear to have a positive impact on endurance performance , even without any improvement in aerobic fitness : by quickly remove metabolic byproduct from your muscle , you be able to sustain a high level of energy production over a long period of time .
biological effect increase level of one protein , however , be probably not the only important effect of sprint training .
in a 2002 review study , , , and at the university of cape town in south africa extensively examine the biological effect of high - intensity sprint training .
a range of study demonstrate increase in performance , accompany by high level of biological marker for anaerobic fitness , fatigue resistance , and power production , but many of these study use untrained individual .
among the study of well - train athlete , sprint training still elicit significant improvement in fitness , but most of the benefit be gain in the first six session of sprint training .
far bout of sprint - style interval workout result in small marginal benefit than the initial six or so , typically spread out over two or three week .
they speculate that highly trained athlete respond more selectively to sprint training than sedentary people : because their fitness be already well - develop , their adaptation to sprint training be mostly in the form of good energy production in the muscle and more efficient processing of metabolic byproduct like lactate .
sprint - style workout , like 7×30 second at near - maximum effort with plenty of recovery be quite different from standard workout for endurance in distance runner .
while these workout might seem like an attractive shortcut to fitness base on study of untrained individual , a well - train distance runner respond much more selectively .
how to incorporate sprint train into your schedule though sprint training can offer distance runner benefit in the form of good management of rise lactate level and high energy production in the muscle , it be not a replacement for the standard workouts that make up the bulk of your training .
to date , scientific research indicate that do around six session of high - intensity sprint training spread out over a few week will net you the big benefit associate with this type of training .
as with everything else in training , if you would like to integrate sprint workout into your routine : you should do it gradually — start with only a couple 15 - 30 second repeat , take ample time to recover between each .
over the course of several week , you could work your way up to more repeat .
do workout base solely on the testimony of a scientific paper can be a risky endeavor because physiology research be an inherently myopic field of study — benefit at four or six week be typically the focus , while long - term result and risk be give relatively less attention .
meaning , do not focus your training schedule on sprint training for a long period of time .
a quick 3 - 5 week segment , especially after a marathon , and a sprint session every few week can get you the benefit you need do not forget that sprint training will put a lot of stress on your body , give the extremely high speed associate with it , and could lead to overuse injury if you do not ease into it .
hopefully , this article provide insight into why sprint training be important and how it will eventually help your training in the long - term , even if you be a marathoner .
remember , develop top end speed take time , especially if you have never do it before .
be patient !
< END > < START > there be not just one style of yoga .

it provide a good physical workout and , unlike some other style of yoga that follow the same series of pose each time , power yoga class be seldom alike .

what be power yoga ?
as the name suggest , power yoga be focus on building strength and endurance .
it be also an excellent form of yoga for burn calorie .
although power yoga be not an official type of yoga , the term be sometimes use interchangeably with vinyasa yoga .
it be probably more accurate to say that power yoga be a form of vinyasa , which have its root in ashtanga yoga , an establish practice that begin in the early 20th century .
with power yoga , the emphasis be on the flow from one pose to the next , rather than approach each pose separately .
the pose be not disconnect from each other , unlike some other form of yoga .
no matter what you call it , power yoga be a fast - pace and intense activity .
you move from one posture to another rapidly , link your breathing to the different motion of your body .
a power yoga class may seem more like an aerobics class than a relaxed , mindful yoga experience .
though it require mindfulness and focus on your breathing , power yoga be more dynamic than meditative .
what be the key difference between power yoga and other type of yoga ?
power yoga differs from other type of yoga in a few important way .
let be look at these difference more closely .
speed unlike yoga , the most common form of yoga practice in the united state , power yoga move at a much faster pace .
yoga focus on pose and breathe at a slow , more deliberate pace than power yoga .
the slow speed of yoga , and other form of yoga that provide a more restorative experience , do not deliver the same cardiovascular exercise benefit as power yoga .
sequence power or vinyasa yoga use many of the same posture as ashtanga yoga , but not always in the same order .
ashtanga yoga be a very precise practice , and each pose be do in the same sequence , no matter who be lead the class .
power yoga class , on the other hand , follow a sequence set by the instructor , or by the individual if you be on your own .
there be more variability and less structure with power yoga .
flow one of the main difference between and vinyasa or power yoga be in the flow .
power yoga emphasize the flow from one pose to the next , exhale as you change position .
yoga be less focus on the flow of pose and more focus on achieve the right posture with each pose .
what be the benefit ?
accord to scientific evidence , power yoga provide a wide range of both mental and physical benefit .
here be a look at some of the key benefit of this fast - flow yoga style .
cardiovascular health because of the fast pace and resistance training involve , research trust source show that power yoga workout can raise and sustain your heart rate .

this , in turn , can help improve your fitness , stamen , and overall health .

be there any drawback ?
power yoga class move at a fast pace and require a certain level of strength and fitness .

it be easy to see why bodybuilding be not often associate with something like yoga , as it focus so much on build muscle mass and strength , and yoga emphasize flexibility , balance , and mindfulness .
one of the primary benefit of yoga for bodybuilder be improved flexibility .
bodybuilder often have tight muscle due to the repetitive motion of weightlift and resistance training .

yoga can directly improve how your muscle perform whilst bodybuilding .
another benefit of yoga for bodybuilder be improved mobility .
many yoga pose require a full range of motion in the joint , which can help to improve joint health and mobility .

finally , a nice addition for those interested in how their physique appear , yoga can help to improve posture and alignment .

ultimately yoga can be a great complementary activity for bodybuilder .
yoga offer numerous physical and mental benefit such as improved flexibility , posture , mobility , stress reduction , and active recovery .

< END > < START > when it come to fitness , much of the focus be put on the workout itself .
want to lose weight ?
a more intense workout can increase your fat burn .
want to build muscle ?
lift heavy weight on strength training day .
but adequate recovery be also important , especially active recovery — and yoga be perfect for this purpose .
the importance of recovery remember that push a muscle to work harder cause tiny tear in the muscle fiber .
it create actual muscle damage .
after a challenge workout , your body needs time to repair this damage .
if time be not give , the muscle can weaken versus strengthen .
the body be unable to recover effectively , and injury can occur .
a lack of adequate recovery can also lead to overtraining .
you can only push the body for so long before it start to break down .
it be the same principle as allow stress to continue to build without release it .
you might not notice the effect at first , but they will eventually appear .
the same be true with exercise .
if you consistently overdo it , it will catch up with you at some point .
an injury can occur to the muscle or surround soft tissue ( ligament , tendon ) if they endure repeat stress with limited recovery time .
overtraining can also lead to stress fracture .
the bone can not sustain all of the physical activity , so it slowly start to break .
a high - intensity workout can also result in delayed onset muscle soreness or doms .
give the body time to recover can help reduce this soreness .
it can also reduce muscle fatigue .
passive recovery v active recovery one way to engage in recovery be to take a rest day .
this be call passive recovery and involve take the day off entirely from any exercise .
passive recovery can be helpful on day when muscle soreness be at its peak .
it be also a good option after complete a reasonably strenuous workout .
another option be to stay active during recovery , though at a low intensity .
this be refer to as active recovery .
research indicate that active recovery offer many benefit .
for instance , a 2019 systematic review note that active recovery positively affect performance ( 1 ) .
it also report that participate in an active recovery session appear to improve psychological outcome .
a previous meta - analysis indicate that active recovery help ease sore muscle ( 2 ) .
some use the term active recovery to describe do less intense exercise between interval train set .
it be also use to reference reduced intensity during a cool down .
for purpose of this article , the phrase “ active recovery ” describe be lightly active on rest day or active rest .
how do active recovery work ?
an active recovery workout help increase blood flow .
blood carry oxygen and many other nutrient that be helpful with recovery to the muscle cell .
light exercise can get the blood move fast than when completely at rest .
this get more of these nutrient to the damage area .
low - intensity movement can also help the body get rid of excess lactic acid .
the more intense your physical exertion , the more lactic acid your body produce .
the national library of medicine share that too much lactic acid can lead to lactic acidosis ( 3 ) .
this cause nausea , weakness , and vomiting .
reduce lactic acid buildup help you avoid these effect .
3 persuasive reason to use yoga for active recovery for an exercise to assist with active recovery , it must be low in intensity .
walking , light swimming , tai chi , and a leisurely bike ride qualify as active recovery exercise .
yoga be another option to consider on an active recovery day .
here be three persuasive reason why .
some yoga style be more intense .
ashtanga and vinyasa yoga be two .
style be slow and aim more toward recovery .
that make them perfect for an active rest day .
restorative yoga be good for an active recovery workout .
yoga and yin yoga be as well .
each of these practice go from pose to pose in a slow , controlled fashion .
the light movement of low - intensity yoga help get the blood flowing .
this make it easy for the body to get nutrient to muscle cell .
these nutrient can be use to well repair muscle damage .
this also impact the amount of soreness you might feel .
the quicker the recovery , the short the duration of your soreness .
part of effective recovery be know what your body need and when .
yoga assist with this by increase body awareness .
you become more in tune with your body .
this make it easy to identify when it might need rest .
it also help avoid overtraining and , subsequently , injury .
additional yoga benefit yoga offer many benefit that extend beyond those associate with active recovery .
john hopkins share quite a few of them , some of which include ( 4 ) : improving strength , balance , and flexibility provide back pain relief ease arthritis symptom increase heart health promote good sleep boost mood reduce stress arguably , each of these yoga benefit also assist with recovery .
this be just one more reason to include yoga on your recovery day .
how often should you engage in active recovery ?
the answer to this question depend on your workout schedule overall .
the more intense your exercise session , the more time you may need to recover from them .
generally speak , most people benefit from take one or two active recovery day per week .
this enable you to meet your fitness goal without over - stress the body .
it be also important to regularly include passive recovery day in your routine .
give your body a day off from any type of exercise so it can relax fully .
your yoga recovery session do not have to be lengthy either .
keep in mind that the goal be not to get a good workout .
it be simply to stay lightly active while give your muscle time to heal .
just 10 - 20 minute of yoga on active recovery day be sufficient for this purpose .

therapeutic benefit of yoga as the popularity of mind - body fitness program , like yoga , continue to grow , it become increasingly important for healthcare professional to be knowledgeable about yoga and its many prove therapeutic benefit .
this article provide helpful information on the therapeutic effect of yoga in various population suffer from a multitude of different ailment and condition .
therapeutic yoga be define as the application of yoga posture and practice to the treatment of health condition .
yoga therapy involve instruction in yogic practice and teaching to prevent , reduce or alleviate structural , physiological , emotional and spiritual pain , suffering or limitation .
yoga be often seek out as a complementary therapy for mental health problem such as depression , anxiety , stress , and insomnia .
the relaxing and grounding nature of yoga can be helpful in shift the balance from the sympathetic nervous system ( cue the body to prepare for fight - or - flight response ) to the parasympathetic nervous system ( which be calm and restorative ) .
some of the way that this calm response manifest physically be low breathing and heart rate .
decrease blood pressure , low cortisol level , and increase blood flow to the intestine and vital organ .
yoga be main goal be to achieve tranquility of the mind , create a sense of well - be , and increase self - confidence while lower irritability .
the practice of yoga also optimize the body be sympathetic response to stressful stimulus .
reduces fear and aggression , and stimulate the pleasure center in the median forebrain .
yoga have be show to be an effective tool in the management of depression .
study have find that regular yoga practice lead to increase in serotonin level and decrease in the level of monamine oxidase and cortisol .
yoga be a safe and natural way to help improve mood and reduce stress and anxiety .
