” < END > < START > hat be proprioception ?
proprioception be a term you may have increasingly hear throw around by doctor and health professional when refer to ‘ body awareness — but what exactly do it mean and how do it affect you ?
it be often refer to as the body be sixth sense after sight , sound , smell , taste and touch .
in short , it be a sense which help inform your body where it be in space and the simple example of it in action be when you close your eye and touch your nose … after all , how do your finger know where your nose be ?
familiar example be when you play the piano ( without have to look at your hand on the key ) , throw a ball ( without have to look at your throw arm ) , and of course , practice yoga ( without have to constantly look at all of your limb ) .
our body be full of sensory receptor call proprioceptor , which be find mainly in our muscle , tendon and skin .
these sensory receptor receive stimulus from within our body that respond to position and movement .
season yogi have a highly developed sense of proprioception as it be a natural extension of be extremely aware of the body and its sensation .
practice yoga require proprioception as you move from pose to pose , maybe stand on one leg in warrior 3 and then open your hip to the side , before transition into half moon and lift your back leg up high .
you be effectively stay upright , whilst often balance on one leg , stretch out your muscle , and move your center of gravity around – without a sense of proprioception , you would certainly fall flat on your face !
example of proprioception in yoga have you ever practice a triangle pose and without thinking , by simply know where all your body part be in relation to one another , automatically pull your torso back in line with your hip , lengthen your spine , and stretch broadly across your chest ?
this , here , be proprioception in action , as you sense your way into the correct alignment without go off balance .
a simpler example be when you step back from the front of your mat into a high lunge without look down at your foot .
your body instinctively know its location , movement and action , which mean you can confidently step back freely without fall over .
a different example be when you pick up a yoga block : you know roughly how much it weigh , thus the proprioceptor in your muscle will automatically know how much strength to use in order to lift it , and you do this without a second thought .
every yoga pose will challenge your sense of proprioception to some degree .
even in the pose which you find be more natural and easy to do , you can still experiment far by practice in a new environment , on a different surface ( grass , sand , thick carpet ) , or simply by close your eye .
how to improve your sense of proprioception if you be new to yoga , you can start with a simple balance pose such as tree pose , use prop or a nearby wall to help you stay steady .
if you be already comfortable with this , challenge yourself by look up towards the ceiling , close your eye , or rotate your torso side to - side .
if you be more experienced with yoga , play around with arm balance such as crow pose or grasshopper pose , where you need to have particularly good control over both your strength and balance .
if arm balance be not for you , find a new yoga pose that you have not do before , which will test your muscle and what they already know .
alternatively , practice yoga in a new space that you be not familiar with , or on a contrast surface to what you be normally use to , which will force your body to adjust .
finally , maintain your proprioception and sense of balance as you age be essential .
if you be not convince , accord to public health england statistic , people age 65 and over have the high risk of fall , which can lead to serious injury or bad .
the numerous balancing pose in yoga provide the perfect challenge for develop your proprioceptive receptor , which will help to keep you healthy and stable as you grow old .
< END > < START > lighten load if you have spend any significant time work to push your performance to the next level , you know that an occasional tweak will happen that create some soreness with exercise .
usually , these tweak though be nothing to worry about , and training can continue as normal .
but what can you do when a more significant injury occurs ?
after month or year of hard work to improve your performance , you ca not just stop training during this injury .
you need to continue train when injure to not only maintain your fitness ( strength , hypertrophy , endurance , etc . )
but to continue improve in whatever way possible .
fortunately , some minor change in your training plan can keep you train without exacerbate tissue heal timeline .
use these tactic as idea to implement to continue train when injure ( not medical advice ) .
five tactic to continue train when injured limit range of motion for many muscle and tendon injury , pain and more damage can happen when the muscle be under tension in a stretched position .
so in these condition , limit the range of motion can be a great way to continue train hard and heavy without slow tissue healing .
for example , in an athlete that have strain his or her pec muscle limit the range of motion with an exercise such as a floor press instead of a bench press can often be enough to allow an athlete to push heavy weight without pain .
deadlifts can be another example of this .
many athlete recover from low back pain have difficulty pull a barbell from the ground .
but deadlifts be a great exercise to use when rehabbing from back pain .
by elevate the bar a few inch off the ground can be a great tactic to continue pull weight , building strength , and work the hip hinge pattern .
use exercise variation small change in the exercise variation we perform can be another great strategy for continued training when injure .
alter your grip , torso angle , knee positioning , etc .
can change the amount of load place on an injured joint or muscle .
let be use the squat as an example .
the front squat typically have a more upright torso versus the back squat .
for many athlete with hip or back pain , this slight change in set up can allow for pain - free training .
for athlete with shoulder pain , subtle change such as change your grip angle can have a positive impact .
switch to a neutral grip with a football bar or dumbbells rather than a barbell with exercise like the bench press or overhead press can very quickly change the pain you feel .
unloaded irritated tissue sometimes we need to unload a tissue to avoid overstrain it completely .
but we can use exercise variation to continue train the surround muscle to continue to improve their strength .
for example , in someone with low back pain not tolerate compressive loading very well or a post - op shoulder , barbell squat variation may not be possible .
the belt squat be one great option to continue load the leg without risk these heal tissue in other area .
a banded hip hinge movement be another excellent example of how we can unload the spine while still push leg loading .
place a resistance band around the hip to resist hip extension .
as the individual become more tolerant of spinal loading , they can add external resistance with barbell or dumbbell to challenge the hip and spine while decrease the band resistance .
i know that we all want to train hard and heavy .
but at time , we ca not push maximal load .
if we have to lift light weight , we simply push up the volume to similar to what we would program in a hypertrophy block .
as the injured tissue heal and tolerate heavier loading , we decrease the volume and increase the weight .
here be an example of how we might progress that over several week : 1st week : 3×25 2nd week : 3×20 3rd week : 3×15 4th week : 5×10 5th week : 5×8 6th week : 5×5 train contralateral in extreme situation , an area may not be able to be load at all .
the best example of this would be after an orthopedic surgery , we frequently have suture hold tissue together .
if overload , the repaired tissue will fail , so we have minimal option for train that area .
in this case , we be go to push train the uninjured side as muscle as possible because research have show that this help us maintain strength and muscle mass on the injured extremity .
while many fear that do this will create a deficit in side to side strength or muscle mass , the opposite appear correct , we will decrease the amount of fitness we lose .
once the healing process progress , we can begin use some of the above strategy to begin rebuild fitness .
< END > < START > unfortunately , thing can happen in life or sport that result in an injury .
injury be a frustrating time for obvious reason , but if you think that an injury mean you must stop training , think again !
if for example you have a fracture in your left arm , you can certainly continue to exercise in the gym .
you can strength train your low body and undertake cycling ( or other form of cardiovascular exercise ) .
another important rehabilitation strategy when you have one side injure be to complete unilateral ( one side ) weight train on your opposite ( uninjured ) side .
people often neglect train the uninjured side which be have show to increase recovery !
but will not train only one side result in significant muscular imbalance ?
accord to numerous study , no .
in fact , research have show that correctly tailor exercise have not only be show to strengthen the uninvolved side but maintain strength and sometimes even muscle mass in the injured limb !
resistance training be a powerful stimulus for neuromuscular adaptation .
( 1 ) these adaptation be not limit to the work muscle and have in fact be show to result in increase in strength and neural drive in a contralateral , rest muscle .
( 1 ) the phenomenon result in this sparing of strength and size on an uninvolved limb be term ‘ cross - education .
( 1 , 2 ) this have be demonstrate in numerous study : they conduct a study on 16 participant whereby the nondominant forearm be immobilize in a cast , while participant be either assign to an exercise group ( eccentric wrist flexion , 3x / week ) or a control group ( no exercise ) for 4 week .
( 2 ) the study find that the resistance training group maintain not only strength , but also muscle cross sectional area of the wrist flexor in the immobilized limb .
( 2 ) furthermore , and colleague conduct a similar study , this time test the effect of exercise on quadriceps strength and muscle activation in an uninvolved limb .
( 3 ) the exercise group exercise their uninjured limb 3x / week for 8 week and the study again conclude that great strength and activation occur in the unexercised limb in the exercise group when compare to the control group .
similarly , a study conduct test the effect of unilateral training to either the left or right leg in 20 previously untrained individual .
( 4 ) the study be conduct over 10 week ( 34 session ) of single - leg exercise complete both the leg press and leg extension .
( 4 ) similarly , this study also conclude that the 10 - week program result in a significant increase in both maximal strength and muscle size in the untrained leg , again demonstrate a cross - education effect .
( 4 ) hence , the research demonstrate the benefit that train an uninjured limb can have on the injured limb .
when you be injure , it be important that you continue with a structured strength train program as your recovery outcome be well .
injury can be a frustrating and demotivating time , especially if you let them keep you away from training .
a tailored exercise routine during a time of injury can still benefit you !
at inspire fitness for well be we adopt this with many of our member in order to keep them on track to achieve their goal .
we do this through our design of individually tailor exercise program that can be shape around a potential injury , in order to keep you active and improve your overall health and well-being .
< END > < START > “ i have injure my “ insert body part ” what can i do ?
” this be the question most people face when injure , and let be firstly state the answer be not just rest !
we have previously discuss the benefit of begin rehabilitation asap on the injured site ( see blog here ) , but what if i tell you that train your uninjured side can result in strength gain on your injured side ?
researcher from the university of copenhagen study the effect of disuse on muscle strength , and reveal in their young subject that two week inactivity result in a staggering 33 percent loss in leg strength , leave them on par with a person who be 40 - 50 year their senior !
and if this be not shock enough , it can take 2 - 3 time as long to regain this lost strength !
fortunately , we have something call the cross - education effect that we can take advantage of !
the cross - education effect be a phenomenon whereby train one side of the body result in an increased strength of the opposite side of the body .
this effect be first observe and publish in the literature over 100 year ago , and since this time there have be hundred of study examine this topic .
what sort of gain can we experience from this cross - education effect ?
the size of contralateral strength gain varies base on the length and type of training , but a 2018 meta - analysis by reveal a strength gain of : 18 percent in young , able - body adult 15 percent in old , able - bodied participant , 29 percent in a patient population consist of post stroke , neuromuscular disorder , and osteoarthritis patient .
this be quite staggering consider this represent 52 - 80 percent of the gain in the trained limb , and it be not even be use !
these effect do not seem to be limit to a single muscle group or area ; benefit have be see all over the body .
how do it happen , and how can we maximize it ?
as yet , researcher have not reach a consensus on the exact mechanism of effect , but the leading theory be that the strength gain on the untrained side be neurally drive .
it be theorize that the cross - over effect be perhaps the body be attempt to strive for symmetry a study examine train parameter ( set / rep / contraction type ) that might maximize the cross - education effect .
they find that perform 3 - 5 set of 8 - 15 repetition of eccentric contraction with rest time of 1 - 2 minute between set , create the great change .
they also find that high - load and more cognitively demand strength training , such as use a metronome to control movement , increase cross - education .
potential us of the cross - education effect any injury that result in an inability to perform your usual resistance training .
some example of its use could include : shoulder pain , and only able to perform 50 percent of your usual bench press and overhead press ?
switch to dumbbell , continue train the uninjured side at 100 percent , and do what you can perform on the injured side break leg and in a cast for 6 week ?
switch to single - leg weight for the uninjured side i.e .
leg press , leg extension , leg curl , split squat , calf raise , to slow the decline in strength of the injured leg .
acute flare - up of knee osteoarthritis ?
train the other leg to take advantage of a 29 percent gain !
shoulder or acl reconstruction ?
early in the rehab process whilst not able to do much on the operated side , keep train the opposite side !
conclusion an injury be not an excuse to stop training do not neglect the uninjured side , use unilateral training to take advantage of the cross - education effect .
cross - education can result in a staggering 18 - 29 percent gain in strength of the opposite side 3 - 5 set of 8 - 15 rep of eccentric contraction with rest time of 1 - 2 minute between set , and also use a metronome when performing may result in a great change .
< END > < START > if you have ever deal with an injury before run in a race or another sporting event , you have probably wonder whether it be safe to continue exercise and training .
although stay less active during recovery can be difficult , exercise while injure can hinder your healing .
here be what you need to know about exercise while deal with a sport injury .
what be a sport injury ?
“ sport injury happen as a result of exercise or other physical activity , . ``
“ they have numerous cause , include overuse , improper technique and a sudden impact .
” sport injury range from minor strain and sprain to more severe condition , like fracture or tear .
while they can occur in any part of the body , sport injury be most common in the knee , ankle and shoulder .
can i exercise while injure ?
determine whether you can exercise while injured depends on the type and severity of your injury .
mild injury like sprain or strain may allow for low - impact exercise such as cycling or swimming .
however , injury like fracture or torn ligament require plenty of rest and proper medical attention .
“ before engage in physical activity after a sport injury , make sure your pain , swell and stiffness be significantly improve , ” say cartwright .
“ push yourself too hard or too soon can exacerbate your injury and slow recovery .
” talk to your doctor about a recovery plan and identify safe exercise while your body heals .
how can i recognize my limit and exercise safely while injure ?
the best way to stay safe be to pay attention to your body and how it feel .
if you experience pain or discomfort during or after exercise , it may be a sign you be overdo it .
start with low - impact exercise , like cycling , walking , swimming or yoga , and gradually increase the intensity as your injury heals .
“ do not train through pain .
if there be pain in the range of motion for that exercise , try decrease the weight or reduce the range of motion .
if neither technique work , then skip that exercise all together , ” say cartwright .
“ talk to your doctor or physical therapist to help determine which exercise and activity be safe for you while your body heals .
” how can i find the motivation to exercise through an injury ?
it can be challenge to stay motivate while injured , but there be thing you can do to help .
“ set realistic goal for yourself and celebrate small victory , ” say cartwright .
“ even low - impact exercise can help you maintain your fitness level and heal from injury .
” find an exercise buddy or join a support group be a great way to keep you accountable and motivate as you regain your footing .
what be some tip for prevent sport injury in the future ?
always warm up and stretch before exercising , which increase blood flow and flexibility and minimize the risk of injury and joint pain .
use proper technique and form help you move more efficiently and lower your risk of injury .
wear appropriate gear and equipment for your workout and stay hydrate throughout .
gradually increase the intensity and duration of your exercise session and take rest day to allow your body to recover .

< END > < START > yoga and stretch for injury prevention and rehabilitation strength , active flexibility , balance , and coordination for reduce injury soft tissue ( joint , muscle , connective tissue ) injury happen when the outside force exceed the force your body can generate in return .
strength the strong your muscle be , the more stable your joint become , directly reduce the likelihood of injury .
strong muscle can withstand more physical stress and protect your joint by absorb the impact that might otherwise strain them .
active flexibility the way active flexibility play a crucial role in reduce the risk of injury be quite similar to strength .
active flexibility mean you have the necessary strength and control of your joint be range of motion .
unlike passive flexibility , where an external force be use to achieve a stretch , active flexibility require your muscular effort .
which in turn help protect the joint against outside force .
active flexibility also enhance your body be proprioceptive ability , which be know where your body part be in space .
as a result , your movement become more controlled and less likely to go beyond safe limit , thereby prevent strain , sprain , and other injury .
balance balance be all about maintain your body be move or stationary position .
have a good balance mean your body can redistribute your weight accord to your movement , which help you avoid fall and stumble that could lead to injury .
a balanced and strong body be also adept at react to change in terrain or direction , which be crucial for avoid misstep that could lead to sprained ankle or similar injury .
coordination coordination be the ability of your body part to work in unison to execute a movement smoothly .
similarly to balance , coordination help you avoid misstep that might put your joint in position where they ca not react quickly enough to counteract the outside force .
yoga and stretching can help us reduce injury and aid recovery .
but the benefit that each practice delivers be different .
how yoga can reduce the risk of injury and aid the rehab although yoga be main aim be to help the practitioner attain harmony and good understand themselves , the physical aspect can also help with injury reduction and recovery .
regularly practice yoga can improve your strength , balance , and coordination .
but yoga alone be not enough to build the strength need to significantly reduce the risk of injury .
for that purpose , strength training and active stretching be more effective .
nevertheless , like any movement , yoga can help restore the range of motion after an injury .
perhaps the great benefit yoga can offer for reduce and rehabbing injury be how it help reduce stress and anxiety .
we know that high level of unmanaged stress and anxiety can reduce pain tolerance and slow recovery after an injury .
low level of stress and anxiety also help you sleep good , allow the body to recover .
both when recover when injured , but also to simply recover between workout .
how stretching can reduce the risk of injury and aid the rehab active stretching be your best bet for reduce the risk of injury .
unlike passive stretching , active stretching help to strengthen your muscle .
and the strong your muscle , the less susceptible they be to injury .
and if you do get injure , the strength you have build with active stretching and strength training will likely reduce the severity of the injury .
moreover , stretch , like yoga , can help restore the range of motion after an injury , make it an integral part of your rehabilitation process .
but again , active stretching take the cake over passive stretching and yoga for restore the range of motion .

what be a muscle strain ?
also know as a pulled or torn muscle , a muscle strain be when the muscle fiber pull apart from each other and be damage .
this can come from put too much weight on the muscle , overuse or fatigue , an accident or use the muscle incorrectly .
the right stretch at the right time be a key component in that treatment plan .

compression and rest can be helpful in a newly strain muscle depend on the severity of the injury .

this can delay the healing process .
do not wait too long to begin stretch .

you should be pain free , back to full strength and flexibility and have complete a slow ramp - up of activity to ensure the area do not feel aggravate .

” sign of overtraining include : fatigue depression sleep disturbances an increase in sickness unresolved muscle soreness if you be suffer from any of these symptom , it be time to speak with your doctor about set a healthy workout schedule and nutrition plan .

suggests use ice for acute swelling or injury , and you can apply heat to the affected area for up to 72 hour follow an injury .
she also suggest light stretch and range of motion exercise , as well as foam rolling , yoga and massage to help stimulate the muscle and increase blood flow .

if you be experience acute pain , especially accompany by swell , it be well to reach out sooner rather than later .

for instance , instead of hold a traditional lunge , try a walking lunge with a twist .

if at any point you experience pain , back down .

“ when start a new exercise routine , take it slow , ” say .
“ do not expect change overnight .

< END > < START > here be 10 modification that you can use to prevent further injury while maintain strength in other area .
you might also want to refresh your memory with more on the subject here : deal with setback — how to stay fit while injure or sick .
1. limit total workout volume .
unless you be an exercise science guru , exercise volume may be a new concept .
we will go over the basic and then show you how to apply it to your workout routine .
exercise calculation , like volume , can be use as a method to measure workout intensity .
generally , volume be calculate use this equation : workout volume = ( the amount of weight that you be lift ) x ( number of set ) x ( repetition ) for example , if you lift 20 lb ( 9 kg ) on the overhead shoulder press for 3 set of 10 repetition , then your workout volume would be ( 20 lb ) x ( 3 set ) x ( 10 rep ) = 600 lb ( 272 kg ) for that particular exercise .
when you be injured , your workout volume should always be less than your pre - injury volume .
to calculate this , modify one ( or all ) of the variable in the above equation .
some example of way in which you can change your training volume include : decrease the number of set you perform limit the number of repetition you do low the amount of weight you lift the good news be that you can work out and maintain fitness level even if you need to temporarily lower your workout volume .
by do so , you be significantly decrease your risk for great injury and reduce the possibility of weakness from inactivity .
2. modify your positioning or lifting technique .
depend on the type of injury you sustain , you may need to modify your body position or lifting technique .
for example , deep squat should be avoid for people with hip , knee , ankle , or low back injury .
instead , take a wide stance and practice mini - squat or wall slide .
people who be recover from shoulder and neck injury should avoid overhead motion and prioritize shoulder stabilization exercise or upper back strengthen .
3. give yourself more time to recover between set .
consider take more time to rest between rep , set , and workout day .
rest period be an underutilized factor when it come to modify an exercise routine , especially while recover from an injury .
many people use short rest period to increase the intensity of the workout ; however , increase the length of the rest period can have the opposite effect ( i.e .
, allow for low intensity ) .
4. focus on unilateral movement to strengthen the weakened area .
unilateral movement be a common term use to describe motion that involve one side of the body .
incorporate them into a workout be an effective way to address weakness and instability in the body .
oftentimes , unilateral movement target important accessory muscle that work to stabilize your body when do large movement .
some example of unilateral movement include : lunge step ups lie leg lift clamshell single leg bridge single leg rdls ( romanian dead lift ) single arm shoulder press bent over dumbbell row dumbbell chest press dumbbell bicep curl 5. consider do different form of exercise while you recover .
look on the bright side : sometimes the `` best `` part of an injury be discover a new activity that you otherwise would have never attempt .
and one of the most effective way to maintain fitness level when you be injure be through something call cross training .
cross training involve participate in similar type of exercise to develop a specific component of fitness .
you may have hear this term reference by marathon runner or triathlon participant , since it be a widely - use method to improve cardiovascular health and endurance .
while these athlete use cross training as a way to rest their body from repetitive motion , you can use it as a way to stay physically active during recovery .
for example , those who be unable to run or jog may prefer to swim or row , since the latter be less jar to the joint in the low body .
similarly , people who suffer from wrist and hand injury may not be able to tolerate cycling and , instead , should jog or go for a brisk walk .
6. work through a pain - free range of motion .
this go without say , but let be take a second to discuss why this be important .
pain with movement be a sign that something be not right .
along with that , any strong , sharp , or persistent pain that develop during exercise should be consider as a red flag and cause for concern .
if you notice pain or discomfort with movement , especially as you be recover from an injury , either stop what you be do or modify your movement .
suggestion on how to modify the movement include change the activity , decrease your range of motion , or limit your rep / set .
7. cautiously reintroduce new exercise .
our body tend to gravitate towards certain pattern of movement .
over time , the body become adept at those particular movement pattern , which increase our vulnerability to injury when do something new .
therefore , when introduce new exercise after an injury , you should move cautiously and with purpose .
the concept of movement pattern be not new , and physical therapist frequently use this principle to help people recover from injury .
you can also take advantage of this by strengthen weaken area of the body use multiple form of the same exercise .
one example of this would be to perform side and reverse lunge in addition to forward lunge .
8. substitute pain - free exercise for painful one be okay .
like cross training , substitute pain - free exercise for painful one be another way to maintain your fitness level as you recover from an injury .
unable to lie flat for bench press ?
strengthen the chest muscle by do an incline press or weight push - ups instead .
sore wrist during plank ?
drop down to your elbow or make a fist .
9. do not be afraid to take some time off .
admittedly , there be time when the modification on this list be not enough .
if that be the case , then it be best to take some time off from exercise or see a specialist .
in the meantime , focus on your body be strengths and exercise that you can perform without pain or limitation .
yoga , walking , and gentle pool exercise be often great alternative to strength or hiit workout .
10. ease back into exercise after recovery .
once you be ready to start exercise again , it be best to ease back into it .
avoid the temptation to load the same amount of weight that you use before the injury , and fight the urge to do your usual rep / set scheme .
gradually reintroduce movement and strengthening exercise be the best way to prevent reinjury .
use low rep and set so you can focus on form , control , and stability .
as always , prioritize core stabilization exercise to ensure that your foundation remain strong and healthy .
final thought .
recover from an injury can be frustrating , but it do not have to signal the end of your workout day .
find way to exercise in a pain - free manner that do not place you at further risk for harm .
use some , or all , of the modification list above , and share your best tip for return from an injury with us below in the comment section .

how can you best stay fit during all that time off ?
no athlete want to be sideline by an injury .
running may be what you love best , but in order to help yourself come back strong time out be essential .
it be extremely important to allow time to heal and focus on a comprehensive rehabilitation program .
if we fail to do his we find ourselves in a vicious circle of early return to activity and re injury .
this make the process a lot long and ultimately far more distressing .
it be vital to honor the body and remember that stay active fit and healthy be something we prioritize for life .
with that important perspective shift we can accept that recovery break be temporary , necessary and vital .
so while the process of rehabilitation take place we can focus on what we can do .
both endurance - orient cross - training and strength work can be use to maintain your aerobic fitness and strengthen the supportive structure that help you move injury - free .
certain type of cross - training such as pool running , cycling and the elliptical be the most effective for aerobic exercise and can support aerobic conditioning for return running .
type of cross - training , such as strength training , swimming and pilate , be more complementary to run .

pool run if you be injured and unable to perform any weight - bearing exercise , aqua jogging should be your go - to method for maintain fitness .

this mean it be most similar to actual running in respect to your movement and biomechanics .

< END > < START > if you be look for an exercise program to help you effectively build mass , you may be look for something to do with hypertrophy training .
similar to classic strength training , the goal of hypertrophy be different .
one focus on building strength and the other on build muscle mass .
hypertrophy be define as `` the enlargement of skeletal muscle fiber in response to be recruit to develop increased level of tension , as see in resistance training .
[ it ] be characterize by an increase in the cross - sectional area of individual muscle fiber result from an increase in myofibril protein ( myofilaments ) .
” specific adaptation to impose demand ( say ) principle state that adaptation be specific to the imposed stimulus .
if the demand be not place on the muscle over time the muscle will begin to atrophy .
what be hypertrophy ?
research indicate that perform approximately 15 - 20 set of challenge hypertrophy exercise per week be the optimum stimulus to enhance muscle size .
since maximal muscle response be achieve through 5 - 6 set of a specific exercise , it be best to spread the workload throughout the week .
this mean that train beyond the maximal growth stimulus you will disrupt the stimulus - recovery - adaptation curve by delay the recovery phase , which be counterproductive to muscle growth .
first , consider a variety of different exercise .
since muscle damage be a function of loading and tension , high tension and high damage exercise will require more time for recovery .
these exercise will also stimulate strong muscle adaptation that will effectively enable it to withstand more tension in subsequent training .
for example , do five set of heavy bench press will cause far more muscle breakdown than 5 set of pushup .
high - tension and high - damage exercise , therefore , require more recovery time but cause great adaptation .
exercise feature an increased range of motion , more time under tension , a great load , and a longer eccentric portion be typically the preferred stimulus to maximize muscle hypertrophy .
muscle hypertrophy be also a function of maximal voluntary isometric contraction and load / unloading .
in other word , the more muscle fiber you can activate through a specific exercise and loading , the great the demand ( stimulus ) and therefore the great the hypertrophy response .
mechanism for hypertrophy & muscular development 1 ) exercise - induced muscle damage during eccentric activity , the contractile element ( actin and myosin ) in work muscle exert a resistance action that produce small tear in both the contractile element and surface membrane ( sarcolemma ) of the associated muscle fiber .
the subsequent muscle repair ( recovery ) strengthen the tissue to protect against further damage ( adaptation ) .
2 ) metabolic stress metabolic stress result from the buildup of various metabolite ( e.g .
, lactic acid , inorganic phosphate , etc . )
, primarily because of training in the fast glycolytic energy system where carbohydrate be use anaerobically to fuel performance .
3 ) mechanical tension ( force ) refer to the amount of force / tension within the muscle fiber in response to a static or dynamic stimulus .
the reaction increase protein synthesis and muscle size .
the goal be to activate as many muscle fiber as possible to maximize the response .
4 ) fascia stretch training pump specific muscle group full of oxygenated blood in a relatively short period of time , force the fascia tissue to stretch and expand like a balloon .
this pack nutrient and oxygen rich blood into and around the muscle cell to promote repair and growth .
speaking of stretch , you can learn more about its relationship with hypertrophy below .
how to train for hypertrophy – rep range and set hypertrophy / muscular development training be typically moderate - heavy loading ( 75 - 85 percent 1rm ) ,6 - 12 rep , 2 - 0 - 2 , 0 - 60 or 0 - 30 rest , 3 - 6 set ( up to 7 ) , 2 - 4 strength exercise per body part .
muscular development podcast ad opt model pyramid set – the volume of set can be modify over time as your training progress .
start out , try shoot for 3 set of a few different exercise for each major muscle group ( or complex movement ) .
for intermediate lifter , increase your set volume to 4 - 6 set .
for advanced lifter or athlete , it be common to see as many as 6 - 7 work set per exercise .
rep – similar to set , rep be an opportunity to manipulate training volume .
for strength hypertrophy , 6 - 12 rep with moderately heavy load 75 - 85 percent 1rm be most effective .
for the best all - around workout , i recommend pyramid up in weight over the course of your work set .
this will maximize hypertrophy and still work the high and low end of the spectrum .
force – loading ( percent 1rm ) time under tension ( tut ) – length of time the muscle stimulus create tension cadence – this be the timing of your concentric and eccentric motion during a lift .
this can vary depend on the specific goal .
for example , stability and strength - endurance type of exercise may use a 4/2/1 ( second ) tempo ( eccentric / isometric stabilization / concentric ) whereas the typical cadence for hypertrophy training be 2/0/2 .
rest interval – another often overlook acute variable be rest interval .
this refer to the rest between set .
for most training , 0 - 60 second be sufficient to replenish 85 to 90 percent of atp and pc and keep your muscle pump up .
for strength endurance and stabilization , 0 - 90 second be recommend .
if you be train for maximal strength / powerlifting , be sure to rest 3 - 5 min between set to ensure your system be fully recover .
vertical v horizontal loading : there be several different way to execute your hypertrophy training .
horizontal loading be the most common .
in horizontal loading , each exercise or muscle group be completely train before move on to the next exercise .
vertical loading be often see in circuit training when each circuit be comprise of a sequence of back - to - back exercise .
( i.e .
, chest press > squat > row , repeat ) .
both have benefit and serve different purpose .
for most hypertrophy training and those chase the pump , horizontal loading be usually the best to keep the specific muscle ( s ) flood with oxygenated blood and nutrient and maximize tension .
progressive overloading : remember , your body be always in a state of adaptation .
you want to improve your cardiovascular performance and vo2 threshold , you will want to stress and challenge that area of the nervous system .
if you want to improve your maximal strength ( i.e .
, powerlifting ) , you will need to train low rep , heavy load to create that specific adaptation .
the key be to shift training phase every 3 - 4 week ( or as need ) to create muscle confusion and force your body to continuously adapt to the stress place upon it .
a decrease in load ( unload ) over an extended period can cause muscle atrophy - a loss in skeletal muscle mass and strength .
with consistent train the body will adapt to the progression and meet the demand of the stress place upon it .
* note that mechanisms such as progressive overload allow you to remain in a specific phase ( i.e .
, hypertrophy / muscular development for bodybuilding ) for long period without risk a plateau .

shoulder exercise with dumbbell 30 best dumbbell exercise of all time 1. goblet squat goblet squat during a dumbbell workout stand with foot shoulder - width apart and hold a heavy dumbbell by its end with both hand at chest , to start .
squat as low as you can , keep back flat and chest up .
at the bottom of the squat , drive through heel to return to start .
that be 1 rep. repeat .
pro tip : you can also try sumo squat , tempo squat , and jump squat ( light weight ) 2. stepup stepup during a dumbbell workout stand perpendicular to a bench or other elevated surface that will put your thigh parallel to the floor when you step on it , to start .
hold a dumbbell in each hand and step up onto the bench , leave your trail leg hanging of .
drive through your front heel to stand .
pause briefly , then slowly low to start position .
that be 1 rep. repeat .
pro tip : you can also stand parallel to the bench and perform lateral stepups 3. turkish getup turkish getup during a dumbbell workout lie faceup on the ground hold a dumbbell in your left hand with arm extend , eye on the weight , leave knee bent with foot plant , to start .
keep your right leg straight out on the ground .
then , push off your left foot , roll onto your right hip and come up onto your right elbow .
push up onto your right hand , and bring your back off the ground .
next , thread your right leg back into a kneeling position .
your arm should still be lock out .
from this kneel position , take a deep breath , tighten your core , and lunge forward to a stand position .
reverse the process to come back down to the start position .
that be 1 rep. repeat .
4. pullover pullover dumbbell exercise lie on your back on the floor and hold a dumbbell by its end overhead with both hand , to start .
press the weight over your chest , then reach back over your head , bend your elbow slightly .
continue until you feel a stretch in your lat , then pull the dumbbell back over your chest .
take a deep breath every time you lower the dumbbell behind you .
that be 1 rep. repeat .
5. walk lunge walk lunge dumbbell exercise stand with foot hip - width apart , hold a dumbbell in each hand , palm face one another , to start .
step forward with one leg and low your body until your rear knee nearly touch the floor and your front thigh be parallel to the floor .
that be 1 rep. step forward with your rear leg to perform the next rep. repeat .
6. lateral lunge lateral lunge during a dumbbell workout stand with foot shoulder - width apart , hold a dumbbell in each hand , palm face one another , to start .

that be 1 rep. repeat , then switch side .

benefit of dumbbell training dumbbell be for everyone — first - time gym goer and professional athlete alike .
if you be wonder why they be so widely use in the fitness industry , rest assure that they be far from a fad .
they be not the be - all , end - all of exercise equipment , but work with dumbbell provide more than a few unique benefit that you should be mindful of .
corrects muscle imbalance by their very nature , dumbbells allow you to work each of your arm or leg independently — as well as the corresponding muscle that move those joint .
this allow you to identify , attack , and remedy any imbalance or side - to - side weaknesses you may have .
while a barbell or fix - path machine can sometimes mask these issue ( since you be move a single piece of resistance with both your arm , for example ) , dumbbell will quickly show you where your weak spot be so you can take the right action against them .
target weak point as the dumbbell be a single - side implement , you can think of it as more of a scalpel than a hammer .
barbell exercise be wonderful for stimulate a lot of muscle quickly and with high load .
man perform concentration curl with dumbbell however , barbell ca not hold a candle to the precise stimulation and resistance offer by a dumbbell .
you would find it difficult , for instance , to properly target your side delts with another type of free weight .
independent movement when work with dumbbell , your limb have more freedom and less restriction than if you use another implement .
this can be particularly helpful when perform exercise such as the bench press , where your individual anatomy strongly impact your form .
no one be perfectly symmetrical side - to - side ; dumbbell allow your body to move as it be design to , rather than have to adhere to a rigid or cumbersome path .
teach motor control single - arm ( or leg ) exercise do a lot more for your body than just stimulate the muscle or muscle in question .
when you load one limb at a time , your body still have to stabilize and control the transfer of force between the weight itself and the surface you be in contact with .
in practical term , this mean that a single - arm press will tax your core as it attempt to stabilize your spine , provide some “ bonus ” ab training .
woman steady dumbbells for overhead press this principle hold true for any movement you opt to perform with , or on , one limb .
build plenty of strength if your priority be maximal strength above all else and at any cost , you should probably spend a lot of time with the barbell — especially if you be aspire toward a strength sport like powerlifting .
bar that , you should not forsake dumbbell in your pursuit of get strong in general .
they will work just fine for strength , even if you be not lift comparably heavy weight as you would in a similar barbell - base movement .
use dumbbell to lift well the equipment you use in the gym be less important than the set and rep you select , which be less important than have motivation to be consistent in the first place .
that say , the devil be in the detail when it come to maximize your fitness potential .
dumbbell should not make up your entire routine ( though they certainly can ) at all time , but they be versatile , customizable , and easy to use .

probably the big benefit be they be versatile and relatively space - efficient , say .
especially after the lockdown , i have a newfound respect for any piece of equipment my client can afford and have space for .
when it come to train with dumbbell vs resistance training machine , many personal trainer will prioritize dumbbell or free weight exercise because they allow for more functional training .
in other word , they allow for the freedom of movement that more closely mimics real - life action .
for example , they will force you to use stabiliser muscle like your core to maintain good form .

in short , yup .

1.bent - over row target : back , glute , biceps a ) stand with both foot flat on the floor and your chest bent towards your foot .

repeat .
2. bicep curl target : arm a ) hold a dumbbell in each hand at your side with palm face forward and arm straight down .
step your foot shoulder - width apart , drive your heel into the ground , bend your knee ever so slightly and brace your core .
b ) lift one dumbbell toward the shoulder , rotate the arm as it move up so that the palm be now face upward .
low your dumbbell to the side and repeat the same movement with the other arm .
remember to exhale when lift your weight and inhale while lower .

c ) then allow the weight to swing back between your leg and repeat .

< END > < START > best barbell exercise barbell back squat barbell front squat barbell romanian deadlift barbell hip thrust barbell overhead press barbell bench press barbell bent - over row back squat back squat be like the holy grail of strength training .
they train one of the most foundational movement pattern human can possibly engage in .
we squat to sit down .
we squat to talk to kid .
we squat to … um … use the facility .
we be literally always squat in day - to - day life .
what muscle do back squat work ?
the primary mover for back squat include all of the muscle involve in hip flexion and extension , which include the quadriceps , hamstring , hip abductor ( glute ) , and hip adductor ( inner thigh ) .
hip extension be the opening or lengthening of your hip , while hip flexion be the closing or shortening of your hip — think bring your knee to your chest ( flexion ) and then put it back down ( extension ) .
your calf , foot , core , back , and even your arm and shoulder engage during barbell back squat .
benefit of back squat barbell back squat be one of the best exercise to help you build strength .
they strengthen your entire posterior chain , teach you how to maintain a strong core , increase hip and ankle mobility , and contribute to muscle growth in your low body .
how to do a back squat : setup : rack a bar on a squat rack or power cage at about shoulder height .
add your weight plate .
start position : unrack the barbell onto your shoulder and take a couple step back from the rack .
stand with your foot shoulder - width apart ( approximately ) ; keep a firm grip on the bar with both hand .
position your gaze forward , take a deep breath , and brace your core .
eccentric ( lower ) phase : keep your eye forward and foot flat on the floor , descend into the bottom of the squat with control .
while ass - to - grass squat be great , we recommend only descend as far as your current mobility allow without your heel peel up from the floor or your chest cave forward .
concentric ( stand ) phase : once you reach your depth , drive through your heel to return to the stand position .
make sure to avoid cave at the knee .
the ascent should be one fluid motion — do not segment the squat by extend your knee before your hip or vice versa .
finish : once you finish your set , walk the bar back to the squat stand and rack it .
woman do back squat front squat front squat just like back squat , front squat be still a foundational movement pattern , except the load be support by the front of your body instead of the backside .
lot of people avoid front squat , and they do so because they just do not like them .
and we ca not blame ‘ em — front squat be painful !
i do not like promote the “ no pain , no gain ” culture , but honestly , you will rarely walk away from a set of front squat without a burn .
just know you will be a good person for it .
what muscle do front squat work ?
the primary mover be the same as for back squat : quad , hamstring , hip abductor , and adductor .
however , you will find that front squat require more core engagement and also tax your shoulder , arm , lat , and upper back significantly more than back squat .
this be due to the front - rack position of the bar .
benefit of the front squat in addition to gain strength and muscle in your leg , front squat have the added benefit of spar your low back from a load it may not be ready for .
by displace the weight onto the anterior ( front ) side of your body , you basically force your body to use your leg and core — not your back — to lift the weight .
how to do the barbell front squat : setup : just like for back squat , rack your barbell on a squat stand or power cage .
you may have to lower the j - cup slightly because you be unracking the bar onto the front of your body now .
start position : unrack the barbell into the front - rack position ( bar rest across front of shoulder ; elbow point forward , palm face upward ; and finger wrap around the top of the bar ) .
position your foot hip- to shoulder - width apart and engage your core .
eccentric ( lower ) phase : just like back squat , descend to your deep range of motion without tip forward or bring your heel up from the ground .
keep your elbow parallel to the ground and your eye forward .
concentric ( stand ) phase : drive through your heel to stand up , push your knee outward to avoid caving in .
finish : fully extend your hip at the top and carefully re - rack the barbell .
barbell romanian deadlift the almighty deadlift : the epitome of “ pick heavy thing up , put them down .
” the deadlift be perhaps the simple , yet still sexy , lift of them all .
do not confuse simplicity with ease , though , amanda warns .
just because the deadlift look easy do not mean it be , and there be actually a lot that can go wrong ( especially when you be go heavy ) .
follow our tip and step - by - step instruction below to master the deadlift .
what muscle do deadlifts work ?
all of them .
every last muscle .
even the tiny one you do not know you have .
if you think you be just work your low back , you be do it wrong .
kid … but not .
when you do deadlifts , you should feel it in your glute and hamstring more than your low back .
and if you be do heavy deadlifts , you will also feel it in your upper back , trap , forearm , core , shoulder , lat , and every other part of your body that help to support the weight of the barbell as you pull it off of the ground .
that say , your primary mover for the deadlift be the muscle responsible for hip extension : hamstring and glute .
relate : best back workouts benefit of the romanian deadlift people who deadlift well can also do a lot of other thing well that the average person struggle with .
take move for example .
how much easy do you think move a couch or a king - sized mattress be for someone who deadlifts versus someone who do not ?
deadlifts develop strength and muscle mass in your hamstring , glute , and back — and more importantly , practice deadlifts teach you how to use that strength safely and properly .
how to do the romanian deadlift : setup : load a barbell with weight plate on the floor .
use standard - size olympic plate for the best deadlift bar setup .
start position : walk up to the barbell like you be about to absolutely hulk - smash it .
position your foot so that the bar hovers over your midfoot and sits close to your shin .
your foot should be stack beneath your hip .
hinge at the hip and grip the barbell ( double overhand grip for badasses and reverse grip for baby … ) with your hand just outside your leg .
concentric ( lift ) phase : drive through your heel and engage your glute and hamstring to pull the weight off of the ground .
keep your spine in the neutral position ( no arching or rounding ) and push your hip forward until you reach full hip extension .
eccentric ( lower ) phase : with control and maintain your neutral spine , low the barbell back to the ground by hinge at your hip , then your knee , to create one fluid motion .
finish : the rep be finish once the weight plat touch the ground ; you can either do touch - and - go rep or reset entirely .
how to do sumo deadlifts : setup : the setup be the same as for conventional deadlifts — use olympic weight plate and load the bar on the ground .
start position : common among powerlifters , sumo deadlifts recruit more from the glute than the hamstring .
assume a wide ( very wide ) stand with your foot .
think about it like you be go to do a stand straddle stretch .
position the bar so it hover above your midfoot and sit very close to your shin .
grip the barbell with your hand shoulder - width apart , in between your leg .
concentric ( lift ) phase : squeeze your glute and pull the bar off the ground use strength from your hamstring and glute .
keep the bar close to your body and pull until you reach full hip extension .
eccentric ( lower ) phase : after you fully stand up with the weight , low it back to the ground .
hip thrust there be one unspoken rule about hip thrust : do not make eye contact with anyone do them .
so it be a good thing you have a home gym because no one will be there to awkwardly shuffle by you as you grunt out your last set of hip thrust .
what muscle do hip thrust work ?
despite be a totally awkward exercise , hip thrust be one of the best for develop low body strength and gaining muscle , specifically in the glute .
all of your glute muscle ( maximus , medius , minimus ) get some action here .
your hamstring also contribute , and your quad , core , and back act as stabilizing and support muscle .
benefit of the hip thrust well , there be the obvious benefit : a nice butt .
a lot of people do hip thrust solely for that reason .
they be arguably the best exercise for target the glute muscle with heavy weight .
however , hip thrust offer non - aesthetic benefit , too .
for starter , they be great for develop the power need for olympic weightlifting ( snatch and clean and jerk ) .
they also play a role in eliminate muscle imbalance , and lot of coach will program them for athlete who display quad dominance .
how to do the hip thrust : setup : you will need a bench or box ( recommend pad a box ) along with your barbell and weight plate .
set up the bench or box so it be sturdy and level .
use a bar pad or fold yoga mat to protect your hip bone from the weight of the bar .
start position : sit on the ground with your upper back rest against the bench .
roll the barbell toward your hip and position it so that it hover above the crease of your hip .
put both hand on the bar ; press your back into the bench ; lift your hip so the barbell hovers above the ground ; and position your foot at a comfortable distance from from the bench , keep them slightly wide than hip - width apart .
concentric ( lift ) phase : squeeze your glute and press your hip upward to lift the barbell .
the range of motion on this exercise be fairly small , so you may not feel like you move very far .
squeeze until your hip fully extend and your body make a bridge with the ground .
be careful not to hyperextend your back .
eccentric ( lower ) phase : slowly low the bar back to the start position by bend your hip .
make sure to keep your foot flat on the floor and keep your core engage throughout the entire movement .
finish : once you finish your set , carefully low yourself and the barbell to the ground and roll the barbell away so you can stand up .
overhead press press it overhead , bring it back down .
simple enough , right ?
actually , many people be surprise to learn that the overhead press be one of the most challenging barbell exercise and that a lot more go into it than simply extension of the arm .
what muscle do overhead press work ?
your deltoid be primarily responsible for press a barbell overhead .
your triceps and pecs also play a role in the pressing motion , while your back muscle ( especially your lat ) help to control the barbell on the descent .
your core and glute should also be isometrically involve the entire time to keep your spine where it need to be .
benefit of overhead press boulder shoulder , dude !
the classic overhead press — also call strict press or military press — develop the delts like few other movement .
in addition to aesthetic , overhead press can help improve shoulder mobility and upper back mobility , as well as strengthen the muscle that protect delicate shoulder joint from damage .
how to do overhead press : setup : set up a bar and weight on a squat stand or power cage at a height you can comfortably unrack it from .
start position : unrack the barbell into the front - rack position and step back from the stand .
plant your foot firmly , take a deep breath , and brace your core .
keep in mind that the front - rack position here be different than in front squat .
for strict press , you will want to point your elbow slightly outward and down at about 45 degree , versus forward and at 90 degree in the front squat .
concentric ( press ) phase : keep your gaze forward and spine neutral ( no hyperextending ) , press the barbell overhead until your elbow fully extend .
eccentric ( lower ) phase : bend at the elbow to lower the bar back to your collarbone — with control , l you wake up with bruise you have to explain to your mom and your significant other .
finish : as soon as the bar make contact with your shoulder / collarbone , you can go in for another rep. when you be do , re - rack the bar or drop it to the hang position ( hold at the hip ) before drop it to the floor .
bench press a staple in powerlifting and bodybuilding alike , the bench press be probably the most dude - bro lift of all time .
this be for good reason : it be one of the most effective exercise for strength and hypertrophy in the upper body .
what muscle do bench press work ?
prime mover during bench press include your pecs , triceps , and anterior deltoid ( front of your shoulder ) .
your lat be involve in the lower portion of the lift .
benefit of the barbell bench press the humble bench press grow your pecs , deltoid , and triceps , and it also shred your serratus muscle — those small muscle that sit atop your upper rib and make you look absolutely shred when they be visible .
more importantly , the bench press improve your upper body push strength , which would come in handy if you ever run out of gas and have to push a car or something .
how to do the barbell bench press : setup : slide your bench into position in the middle of your power rack .
rack the barbell and weight at a height you can comfortably reach from the bench .
start position : positioning for bench press vary a lot among people , but in general , you should situate yourself on the bench so that you can reach the bar without lock out your elbow ( because you will need some leverage to unrack it ) , and so that your foot can touch the floor .
grip position varies base on anatomy and preference , but should fall around shoulder - width .
eccentric ( lower ) phase : unrack the bar and hold it above your chest with your elbow fully extend .
keep your wrist strong , bend at the elbow to lower the barbell until it touch your chest .
the barbell should make contact somewhere between the low pec muscle and sternum .
generally , the narrow your grip , the low on your torso that contact point will be .
concentric ( press ) phase : recruit your pecs , shoulder , and triceps to press the bar back up to the start position .
finish : the rep be complete when your elbow fully extend .
rerack the bar by guide it backward into the j - cup on your power rack .
woman do bench press bent over row bent - over row be a must - have in your routine for strong , develop back muscle .
they be simple but effective .
what muscle do bent - over row work ?
your lat and spinal erector muscle be the main mover for the barbell bent - over row .
many other muscle directly support the rowing movement pattern , include your rhomboid ( which retract your shoulder blade ) , trap ( which depress and raise your shoulder blade ) , your deltoid , biceps , and other small muscle throughout your back .
your hip and glute be engage isometrically while you be in the hip - hinge position .
benefit of the barbell bent - over row bent - over row be ideal for increase strength in your upper and mid - back , which can transfer to the skill you need for movement like pull - ups .
develop those upper and mid - back muscle also assist your ability to hold onto the bar during heavy deadlifts and complete the pull - on power clean and snatch .
how to do the barbell bent - over row : setup : load a barbell on the ground with olympic weight plate .
start position : stand with your foot beneath the barbell as if you be set up for a deadlift .
grab the bar with a double overhand grip ( double underhand if you want to target more biceps and rhomboid ) , with your hand shoulder - width apart and palm face down .
you should be in a hip - hinge position with your back straight .
concentric ( row ) phase : think about squeeze your shoulder blades together .
pull the barbell toward your torso and try to tap it to your sternum .
your elbow should travel backward and point to the sky behind you .
palm remain face down .
eccentric ( lower ) phase : extend your arm to lower the barbell back to the start position .
finish : there be no real resetting for this exercise ; simply go in for another rep after you lower the bar .

15 best barbell exercise barbell back squat barbell front squat barbell bench press barbell rack pull barbell romanian deadlift barbell bent over row barbell push press barbell hip thrust barbell floor press barbell biceps curl barbell hang clean barbell good morning barbell kirk shrug barbell overhead carry barbell skull crusher 1. barbell back squat the back squat be call the “ king of all exercise ” for a reason .
squat with a heavy barbell on your back allow you to overload your leg muscle with more weight than you could with other tool .
your core work overtime as you brace to ensure that your torso be rigid throughout the movement ( which promote a stable and safe spine ) .
and your back , which be support the physical load , will also reap some strength gain .
back squat be also great for both heavy , low - rep training or lighter , high - rep training .
high rep squat ( and low rep but not to the same extent ) cause the body to produce more growth hormone that trigger the effect of increase your overall size and strength , as well as improve your explosive power .
( 1 ) ( 2 ) how to do it step under a barbell and set a good foundation by flex your core to lift the barbell off the squat rack .
grip the barbell wherever allow you optimal shoulder mobility to get your elbow under the bar .
set it either high or low on your upper back , unrack it , and take a few step back .
pull the bar down into your shoulder to create tension .
keep your chest up , take a deep breath in and squat down to a comfortable depth and pause for a beat .
drive your foot through the floor until lockout .
coach be tip : take time to experiment with stance width and foot position to find something comfortable for you .
set and rep : try 3 set of 6 - 8 reps. 2. barbell front squat you may be think , “ wait , do we really need two squat on this list ?
” yes , and here be why : though they be both squat pattern , the front squat have you support the barbell in the front rack position , rest across your shoulder .
this position take the load off your back , reduce spinal compression , and force you to contract your upper back muscle well to prevent the bar from fall forward mid - lift .
compare to the back squat , the front squat train the body be anterior muscle more heavily , engage the quad and anterior core to a great degree .
how to do it assume a proper front rack position by put the barbell high up onto the shoulder , ensure the bar be support with the shoulder and upper chest .
keep your shoulder down and chest up and take three step back from the rack .
descend into a squat keep the back in neutral while minimize forward lean of the torso .
once you have hit the bottom position , push through the whole foot and stand up , maintain an upright torso , chest , and forward elbow position .
coach be tip : think about “ show your armpit ” to the mirror in front of you to maintain your front rack .
set and rep : go for 3 set of 8 to 10 reps. 3. barbell rack pull the rack pull be a deadlift variation similar that train all the same muscle in the standard deadlift but with a reduced range of motion ( rom ) .
for rack pull , you start with the barbell at or just below knee height .
you can elevate the barbell on block , weight plate , or the safety arm of a power rack .
because of the reduced range of motion , it be easy to maintain a neutral spine .
plus , you can use more weight with the rack pull , so it both acclimate your body to handle heavy load and strengthen the top half — or lockout — of your deadlift .
how to do it set the barbell up in the squat rack either above or below the knee .
assume your standard deadlift stance and grip .
hinge down and grip the barbell with an overhand shoulder - width grip and squeeze your armpit together , keep your chest up and shoulder back .
pull up until lockout , finish with your glute .
hinge back to the start position and repeat .
coach be tip : go hard and heavy here , work with more weight than you can deadlift from the floor .
set and rep : do 4 to 5 set of 3 to 5 reps. 4. barbell romanian deadlift this be our second deadlift variation on the list , and there be a reason we choose both over the conventional version .
regard the romanian deadlift , it be a bit more specific and beginner - friendly ( similar to the rack pull . )
the move be visually very similar to the standard deadlift , but the rdl have you low the bar to about mid - shin level instead of back to the floor .
this slight tweak keep tension on the glute and hamstring muscle , make it a good option to isolate those area and on the low back .
a strong low back will carry over to your deadlift and help prevent spinal rounding ( or cat - back ) during heavy pull .
the rdl be also generally safer as it do not allow you to use much weight as your standard deadlift .
how to do it stand tall with your foot hip - distance apart and grip the barbell with an overhand grip in front of the thigh .
with your chest up and shoulder down , take a deep breath in and hip hinge until the barbell be below your knee .
always keep the barbell close to your body .
pause for a second and exhale and use your hamstring and glute to pull you back to a stand position .
reset and repeat .
coach be tip : think about push your butt back toward an invisible wall behind you while you hinge .
set and rep : try 2 or 3 set of 8 to 12 repetition .
5. barbell bench press the bench press and all its variation ( incline , decline , close - grip , with dumbbell , and the floor press ) target the chest , triceps , and shoulder .
like most barbell exercise , it allow you to use a great load ( because of the relatively straight bar path and the stability of the bench ) than you could muster with kettlebells or dumbbell .
for powerlifters , this move be a must - do as it be one of the three main competition lift ( the other two be the back squat and deadlift ) .
how to do it lie flat on your back on a weight bench and get your eye directly underneath the barbell .
grip the bar with hand wider than shoulder - width apart with a neutral wrist .
bring your foot closer to your glute , push your foot back and un - rack the bar in the lockout position .
then bring the bar slowly down to your chest , pause for a moment , and press it back to the start position .
coach be tip : the bar path of a bench press be not straight up and straight down ; press up and backward slightly so the bar end directly over your shoulder .
set and rep : try 4 set of 8 reps. 6. barbell bent - over row the bent over row be a fantastic exercise to strengthen and increase mass in the upper back and lat and reinforce good hip hinge mechanic .
because you be in a hip hinge position , this train the low back isometrically , make it a great accessory exercise to improve your deadlift .
bent - over row the bent - over row be a horizontal row variation that allow you to use the most weight .
in most case , more weight equal more muscle and strength .
how to do it put a loaded barbell on the floor stand with your foot slightly more than hip - width apart .
hinge down to the barbell and grab the barbell with a shoulder - width grip .
then bring the barbell up to knee level with back straight and torso bent at 45 degree .
pull the barbell to between your navel and sternum .
pause , then slowly low the barbell back down and repeat .
coach be tip : your torso should be between parallel to the floor and a 45 - degree angle .
set and rep : try 3 or 4 set of 8 to 12 reps. 7. barbell push press the overhead press be a fantastic shoulder exercise , no doubt .
but how often do you find yourself not move your low body to get something overhead ?
the push press use the triple extension of the ankle , knee , and hip , which closely mimic what most overhead athlete do on the field and you do at home or the gym .
plus , the low body dip allow you to lift more weight overhead than the barbell overhead press .
lift more weight overhead allow for more muscle and strength .
how to do it stand in front of a loaded barbell , set to about chin - height in a power rack .
grab the bar with a grip that be slightly wide than shoulder - width .
brace your ab , dip your knee a little bit , and then explosively push the bar overhead .
catch the bar gently on your chest and then repeat .
coach be tip : think about initiate the movement with just your leg and press with your arm only after the bar clear your head .
set and rep : go for 4 to 5 set of 3 to 5 reps. 8. barbell hip thrust use the hip thrust will build both strength and mass in your glute .
though the glute be work during the back squat and deadlift , the hip thrust be as close to an isolation movement as exists for the glute .
a person do the hip thrust exercise in the barbed gym .
and hone in on the glute will carry over to those movement and make you a more efficient runner , jumper , and sprinter .
plus , you will look great in your favorite pair of pant .
how to do it sit with your back up against the edge of a bench that be parallel to you .
with pad across your pelvis , roll a loaded barbell into the crease of your hip .
once the barbell be secure , drive your foot and back towards the bench .
you want your shoulder blade to be on the bench and upper body and hip in a straight line .
keep your upper body steady as you low your hip toward the ground and when extend into lockout .
coach be tip : actively drive your upper back against the bench as you thrust .
set and rep : do 4 set of 12 to 15 reps. 9. barbell floor press the barbell floor press be a great option for lifter look to strengthen the top portion of their press .
by press a barbell from the floor , you be limit your range of motion and focus more on triceps and lockout strength .
this mean you can typically press more weight than other dumbbell bench press variation .
that can equate to a strong bench press and big triceps .
this be always a great option when all the bench be take , or you need to work around shoulder issue .
how to do it lie down in front of a power rack .
extend your arm .
adjust the hook so that the barbell sit where your hand reach .
plant your foot firmly on the floor .
grab the bar with your typical bench press grip .
lift the bar out of the rack .
low it to your sternum .
keep your elbow tuck in at 45 degree .
press back up .
coach be tip : low the weight down until your elbow barely touch the floor .
make gentle contact .
set and rep : try 2 set of 12 to 15 reps. 10. barbell biceps curl there be many biceps curl variation , but the barbell biceps curl be the granddaddy of them all .
if your wrist and elbow be healthy , this variation will allow you to curl more weight and increase strength and mass .
bicep strength play an important role in pull from the floor and row and pull - up variation .
if your biceps be a weak link , then you will not get the best out of these exercise .
strengthen them allow you to build more strength and mass with these pull exercise .
how to do it hold a barbell with an underhand grip .
your hand should be slightly wide than hip - width .
keep your shoulder back and down .
curl the barbell up towards your shoulder .
let your elbow drift forward while lock your shoulder in place .
pause and squeeze your biceps at lockout .
slowly low , keep a tall posture .
reset and repeat .
coach be tip : keep your upper arm pin tightly to your side and do not sway at the hip .
set and rep : do 4 set of 6 to 8 repetition .
11. barbell hang clean the hang clean be similar to the power clean , which be a staple in most high school , college , and professional weight room .
but the hang clean have a shorter learn curve .
this be because you will generate power from a friendly low back position .
a person do barbell hang clean exercise in the barbed gym .
this exercise still require a powerful hip drive , a strong pull , and dip and catch — just like the power clean .
and the hang clean will still build slab of upper back strength and mass .
plus , it be less stressful on the low back , which be great if you tend toward low back pain .
how to do it stand tall with the barbell at arm be length with an overhand grip .
place your foot shoulder - width apart .
hinge at your hip until the bar be at knee height .
push your foot into the floor and explosively pull the barbell .
keep your chest up and the barbell close to your body .
pull until the bell be in your hip crease .
snap your hip forward and pull the bar up to your shoulder .
as the bar continue up , drop into a squat .
catch the bar in the front rack position .
your elbow should be up and face forward .
the barbell should be at your collarbone .
squat up until lockout .
reset and repeat .
coach be tip : maintain balance foot pressure as you hang , do not sit back too far onto your heel .
set and rep : go for 4 to 5 set of 2 to 4 repetition .
12. barbell good morning barbell good morning be a fantastic move that train the low back , glute , and hamstring all at once .
this exercise need to be master with light load before increase intensity and range of motion .
when you do it right , this exercise will build and strengthen posterior chain .
in turn , this will help build a strong and healthy squat and deadlift performance .
how to do it step into a squat rack .
unrack the barbell on your trap .
walk out two or three step .
hinge at your hip with a slight bend in your knee .
keep your chest up and shoulder down .
hinge until your torso be almost parallel to the floor .
contract your glute and hamstring to lift yourself to a stand position .
reset and repeat for reps. coach be tip : start with less weight than you think you need for good morning .
set and rep : try 2 set of 15 repetition to begin with .
13. barbell kirk shrug shrug get their name from the guy who first use them , world champion powerlifter .
he start do this shrug variation to improve his grip strength for the deadlift .
because this shrug variation use a thumbless grip , the focus be on the upper back and grip strength .
yes , it improve his deadlift , but it build an impressive yoke , too .

how to do it place a barbell at thigh height in a squat rack .

keep your shoulder down and your chest up .
pause for a second at the navel .
slowly low the barbell down to the start position .
coach be tip : lean forward slightly to increase your range of motion .
set and rep : do 2 or 3 set of 15 to 20 repetition .
14. barbell overhead carry all carry variation be great , but the barbell overhead carry take carry to a whole new level .

a person do perform the barbell overhead carry exercise .
your upper back and trap get serious time under tension for improved muscle and strength .

take slow , deliberate step .

15. barbell skull crusher the barbell skull crusher have you low a barbell to your forehead to stretch the triceps muscle before you contract it .
